45.01Â Â Â PERSONS UNDER LEGAL AGE.
As used in this section, â€œlegal ageâ€ means 21 years of age or more.
1.Â Â Â A person or persons under legal age shall not purchase or attempt to
purchase, consume, or individually or jointly have alcoholic beverages in their
possession or control; except in the case of any alcoholic beverage given or
dispensed to a person under legal age within a private home and with the
knowledge, presence, and consent of the parent or guardian, for beverage or
medicinal purposes or as administered to the person by either a physician or
dentist for medicinal purposes and except to the extent that a person under
legal age may handle alcoholic beverages during the regular course of the
personâ€™s employment by a retail alcohol licensee, or wine or beer permittee
under State laws.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 123.47[3])
2.Â Â Â A person under legal age shall not misrepresent the personâ€™s age for the
purpose of purchasing or attempting to purchase any alcoholic beverage from any
retail alcohol licensee or wine or beer permittee.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 123.49[3])
45.02Â Â Â PUBLIC CONSUMPTION OR INTOXICATION.
1.Â Â Â As used in this section unless the context otherwise requires:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â â€œArrestâ€ means the same as defined in Section 804.5 of the Code of Iowa
and includes taking into custody pursuant to Section 232.19 of the Code of
Iowa.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â â€œChemical testâ€ means a test of a personâ€™s blood, breath, or urine to
determine the percentage of alcohol present by a qualified person using devices
and methods approved by the Commissioner of Public Safety.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â â€œPeace officerâ€ means the same as defined in Section 801.4 of the Code
of Iowa.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â â€œSchoolâ€ means a public or private school or that portion of a public
or private school that provides teaching for any grade from kindergarten
through grade twelve.
2.Â Â Â A person shall not use or consume alcoholic liquor, wine, or beer upon the
public streets or highways. A person shall not use or consume alcoholic liquor
in any public place, except premises covered by a retail alcohol license. A
person shall not possess or consume alcoholic liquors, wine, or beer on public
school property or while attending any public or private school-related
function. A person shall not be intoxicated in a public place.
3.Â Â Â A person shall not simulate intoxication in a public place.
4.Â Â Â When a peace officer arrests a person on a charge of public intoxication
under this section, the peace officer shall inform the person that the person
may have a chemical test administered at the personâ€™s own expense. If a device
approved by the Commissioner of Public Safety for testing a sample of a
personâ€™s breath to determine the personâ€™s blood alcohol concentration is
available, that is the only test that need be offered the person arrested. In a
prosecution for public intoxication, evidence of the results of a chemical test
performed under this subsection is admissible upon proof of a proper
foundation. The percentage of alcohol present in a personâ€™s blood, breath, or
urine established by the results of a chemical test performed within two hours
after the personâ€™s arrest on a charge of public intoxication is presumed to be
the percentage of alcohol present at the time of arrest.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 123.46)
45.03Â Â Â OPEN CONTAINERS IN MOTOR VEHICLES.
[See Section
62.01(50) and (51) of this Code of Ordinances.]
45.04Â Â Â SOCIAL HOST.
A person who is the owner or lessee of, or who otherwise has control over,
property that is not a licensed premises shall not knowingly permit any person,
knowing or having reasonable cause to believe the person to be under the age of
18, to consume or possess on such property any alcoholic beverage. The
provisions of this subsection shall not apply to a landlord or manager of the
property or to a person under legal age who consumes or possesses any alcoholic
beverage in connection with a religious observance, ceremony, or rite.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 123.47)

46.01Â Â Â CURFEW.
1.Â Â Â Purpose.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The Council has determined that there has been an increase in juvenile
violence and crime by persons age 17 and under in the City; and
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Persons age 17 and under are particularly susceptible by their lack of
maturity and experience to participate in unlawful and gang-related activities
and to be victims of older perpetrators of crime; and
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The City has an obligation to provide for the protection of minors from
each other and from other persons for the enforcement of parental control over
and responsibility for children, for the protection of the general public and
for the reduction of the incidence of juvenile criminal activities.
2.Â Â Â Definitions. For use in this section, the following terms are defined:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â â€œCurfew hoursâ€ means 10:30 p.m. until 5:00 a.m. each day.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â â€œEmergencyâ€ means an unforeseen combination of circumstances or the
resulting state that calls for immediate action. The term includes, but is not
limited to, a fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any
situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss
of life.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â â€œEstablishmentâ€ means any privately owned place of business operated
for a profit to which the public is invited, including but not limited to any
place of amusement or entertainment.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â â€œGuardianâ€ means:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â A person who, under court order, is the guardian of the person of a
minor; or
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by a
court.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â â€œMinorâ€ means any person 17 years of age or under.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â â€œOperatorâ€ means any person operating, managing, or conducting any
establishment including the members or partners of an association or
partnership and the officers of a corporation.
Â Â Â G.Â Â Â â€œParentâ€ means a person who is:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â A biological parent, adoptive parent or step-parent of another
person; or
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â At least 18 years of age and authorized by a parent or guardian to
have the care and custody of a minor.
Â Â Â H.Â Â Â â€œPublic placeâ€ means any place to which the public or a substantial
group of the public has access and includes but is not limited to streets,
highways and the common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment houses, office
buildings, transport facilities and shops.
Â Â Â I.Â Â Â â€œRemainâ€ means:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â To linger or stay; or
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â To fail to leave the premises when requested to do so by a police
officer or the owner, operator, or other person in control of the premises.
Â Â Â J.Â Â Â â€œSerious bodily injuryâ€ means bodily injury that creates a substantial
risk of death or that causes death, serious permanent disfigurement or
protracted loss or impairment of the function of any bodily member or organ.
3.Â Â Â Offenses.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â A minor commits an offense if they remain in any public place or on the
premises of any establishment within the City during curfew hours.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A parent or guardian commits an offense if they knowingly permit or by
insufficient control allows the minor to remain in any public place or on the
premises of any establishment within the City during curfew hours.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The owner, operator, or any employee of an establishment commits an
offense if they knowingly allow a minor to remain upon the premises of the
establishment during curfew hours.
4.Â Â Â Defenses.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â It is a defense to prosecution under subsection 3 of this section that
the minor was:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â Accompanied by the minorâ€™s parent or guardian;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â On an errand at the direction of the minorâ€™s parent or guardian,
without any detour or stop;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (3)Â Â Â In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (4)Â Â Â Engaged in an employment activity or going to or returning home
from an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (5)Â Â Â Involved in an emergency;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (6)Â Â Â On the sidewalk abutting the minorâ€™s residence or abutting the
residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the
Police Department about the minorâ€™s presence;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (7)Â Â Â Attending or traveling to or from, without any detour or stop, an
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the City, a school, a religious
organization, a civic organization, or any similar entity that takes
responsibility for the minor;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (8)Â Â Â Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States
Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech and the
right of assembly.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â It is a defense to prosecution under Subsection 3(C) of this section
that the owner, operator, or employee of an establishment promptly notified the
Police Department that a minor was present on the premises of the establishment
during curfew hours and refused to leave.
5.Â Â Â Enforcement.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Before taking any enforcement action under this section, a police
officer shall ask the apparent offenderâ€™s age and reason for being in the
public place. The officer shall not issue a citation or make an arrest under
this section unless the officer reasonably believes that an offense has
occurred and that, based on the minorâ€™s response and other circumstances, no
defense in Subsection 4 of this section is present.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A minor who is in violation of this section shall be reunited with the
minorâ€™s parent or guardian or custodian or other adult taking the place of the
parent or may be taken home by the police officers of the City
6.Â Â Â Penalty, Municipal Infraction. A violation of this section shall be a
municipal infraction with penalties not to exceed those contained in
Chapter 3 of this Code of Ordinances.
46.02Â Â Â CIGARETTES AND TOBACCO.
It is unlawful for any person under 21 years of age to smoke, use, possess,
purchase, or attempt to purchase any tobacco, tobacco products, alternative
nicotine products, vapor products, or cigarettes. Possession of tobacco,
tobacco products, alternative nicotine products, vapor products, or cigarettes
by an individual under 21 years of age shall not constitute a violation of this
section if the individual under 21 years of age possesses the tobacco, tobacco
products, alternative nicotine products, vapor products, or cigarettes as part
of the personâ€™s employment and said person is employed by a person who holds a
valid permit under Chapter 453A of the Code of Iowa or who lawfully offers for
sale or sells cigarettes or tobacco products.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 453A.2)
46.03Â Â Â CONTRIBUTING TO DELINQUENCY.
It is unlawful for any person to encourage any child under 18 years of age to
commit any act of delinquency.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 709A.1)
CHAPTER 47
PARK REGULATIONS
Â 
47.01 Purpose    47.03 Fires
47.02 Park Rules
Â 
47.01Â Â Â PURPOSE.
The purpose of this chapter is to facilitate the enjoyment of park facilities
by the general public.
47.02Â Â Â PARK RULES.
The following rules shall be observed by persons in the public parks and
playgrounds in the City.
1.Â Â Â Motor Vehicles. Unless authorized by the Mayor and Council, no person
shall drive a motor vehicle, motorcycle, motor scooter, snowmobile, or other
vehicle of similar nature, except on the established roads and ways and then
only at a moderate rate of speed and at no time at a speed greater than 10 MPH.
2.Â Â Â Parking. Motor vehicles shall not be parked in such manner to obstruct the
roadway, and unless otherwise designed by signs, shall be parked parallel with
the roadway and with not more than two wheels off the roadway.
3.Â Â Â Littering. No person shall litter the grounds with any form of waste
material. All litter, papers, and refuse must be deposited in the receptacles
provided, therefore.
4.Â Â Â Conduct. No person shall use any loud, violent, obscene, or profane
language while in any park or playground, or conduct themselves in a disorderly
or obscene manner, or commit any nuisance upon the grounds.
5.Â Â Â Improvements, Animals, and Plants. No person shall disturb or interfere
with any improvements made in or about the parks and playgrounds or disturb or
interfere with birds, animals, fish, flowers, or plants kept or found therein.
6.Â Â Â Trespassing. No person shall enter upon portions of the grounds in
disregard of signs or notices posted by the Department of Parks and Public
Property forbidding the same.
7.Â Â Â Commercial Activity. No services shall be rendered or merchandise sold or
delivered or made available for pecuniary profit, or business of any kind
transacted, or entertainment given in any park or playground without first
obtaining permission from the Mayor and Council.
8.Â Â Â Parties and Assemblages. Picnic parties, assemblages for persons, and any
business or entertainment permitted in any park shall occupy grounds designated
by the Superintendent and shall be under the Superintendentâ€™s control and
supervision.
9.Â Â Â Commercial Vehicles. Except as permitted by the Superintendent, commercial
vehicles are excluded from all park and playground roads and ways.
10.Â Â Â Golf. No person shall play, practice, or otherwise hit a golf ball in any
manner in any park or playground, except in areas specifically designated by
the Superintendent and marked with appropriate signs specifying the places golf
balls may be hit.
11.Â Â Â Horses. No horseback riding shall be permitted, except in areas and on
trails designated by the Superintendent and so marked with appropriate signs.
12.Â Â Â Parking Regulations. The Mayor and Council shall designate parking areas
and make such parking regulations in the parks and playgrounds as they shall
deem necessary, and after appropriate signs have been posted notifying the
public, no person shall violate the instructions of such signs.
13.Â Â Â Trees and Shrubs. The Superintendent shall have charge of all trees and
shrubs growing in any park, playground, or public place, and shall plant, care
for and maintain, or remove such trees and shrubs.
14.Â Â Â Planting, Removal, or Treatment of Trees and Shrubs. No person shall
plant, move, spray, fertilize, brace, trim, cut, or otherwise disturb any tree
or shrub in any park, playground, or public place without first obtaining a
written permit from the Clerk. Such work shall be done under the supervision of
the Superintendent. Every permit shall describe the work to be done, the
species, sizes, and locations of trees and shrubs concerned, and the date of
expiration. Any permit may be declared void if its terms are violated.
15.Â Â Â Signs, Wires, Etc. No person shall fasten any sign, box, wire, rope, or
other material to any tree or shrub in any park, playground, or public place
except by permission of the Department of Parks and Public Property.
16.Â Â Â Protection of Root Systems. No person shall place or maintain upon any
park, playground, or public place any material which may impede the free
passage of water, air, and fertilizer to the roots of any tree or shrub growing
therein, except by permission of the Department of Parks and Public Property,
or when such materials are designed for the construction of sidewalks, paving,
gutters, or other public improvement and have been placed under a permit
granted by the City.
17.Â Â Â Injury to Property. No person shall break, deface, injure, or destroy any
tree or shrub in any park, playground, or public place. No person shall
knowingly permit any leak to exist in any gas pipe or main within the root zone
of any such tree or shrub unless protected by approved methods. Whenever the
Superintendent determines it to be necessary in order to prune or remove any
tree or shrub to protect, move, or cut off the electricity from any service
wire, the Superintendent shall serve written notice on the owner of such wire
to protect such wire and the owner shall comply with such order within 24 hours
after service of the notice.
18.Â Â Â Parks Closed. All public parks and playgrounds shall be closed from 10:30
p.m. to 6:00 a.m. on each day. Any person other than a municipal employee on
duty, law enforcement officer, or other person duly authorized by the
Superintendent, Mayor, or Council, entering or being in a public park or
playground during the hours the park or playground is closed shall be in
violation of this Code.
19.Â Â Â Additional Rules. The Council may make such additional regulations by
resolution as it may deem necessary and after such regulations have been posted
in appropriate places notifying the public thereof, no person shall violate the
instructions of such signs.
47.03Â Â Â FIRES.
No fire shall be built, except in a place designated for such purpose, and such
fire shall be extinguished before leaving the area unless it is to be
immediately used by some other party.

50.01Â Â Â DEFINITION OF NUISANCE.
Whatever is injurious to health, indecent, or unreasonably offensive to the
senses, or an obstruction to the free use of property so as essentially to
interfere unreasonably with the comfortable enjoyment of life or property is a
nuisance.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 657.1)
50.02Â Â Â NUISANCES ENUMERATED.
The following subsections include, but do not limit, the conditions that are
deemed to be nuisances in the City:
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 657.2)
1.Â Â Â Offensive Smells. Erecting, continuing, or using any building or other
place for the exercise of any trade, employment, or manufacture that, by
occasioning noxious exhalations, unreasonably offensive smells, or other
annoyances, becomes injurious and dangerous to the health, comfort, or property
of individuals or the public.
2.Â Â Â Filth or Noisome Substance. Causing or suffering any offal, filth, or
noisome substance to be collected or to remain in any place to the prejudice of
others.
3.Â Â Â Impeding Passage of Navigable River. Obstructing or impeding without legal
authority the passage of any navigable river, harbor, or collection of water.
4.Â Â Â Water Pollution. Corrupting or rendering unwholesome or impure the water
of any river, stream, or pond, or unlawfully diverting the same from its
natural course or state, to the injury or prejudice of others.
5.Â Â Â Blocking Public and Private Ways. Obstructing or encumbering, by fences,
buildings or otherwise, the public roads, private ways, streets, alleys,
commons, landing places, or burying grounds.
6.Â Â Â Houses of Ill Fame. Houses of ill fame, kept for the purpose of
prostitution and lewdness; gambling houses; places resorted to by persons
participating in criminal gang activity prohibited by Chapter 723A of the Code
of Iowa or places resorted to by persons using controlled substances, as
defined in Section 124.101 of the Code of Iowa, in violation of law, or houses
where drunkenness, quarreling, fighting, or breaches of the peace are carried
on or permitted to the disturbance of others.
7.Â Â Â Billboards. Billboards, signboards, and advertising signs, whether erected
and constructed on public or private property, that so obstruct and impair the
view of any portion or part of a public street, avenue, highway, boulevard, or
alley or of a railroad or street railway track as to render dangerous the use
thereof. (See also Section
62.06)Â 
8.Â Â Â Storing of Flammable Junk. Depositing or storing of flammable junk, such
as old rags, rope, cordage, rubber, bones, and paper, by dealers in such
articles within the fire limits of the City, unless in a building of fireproof
construction.
9.Â Â Â Air Pollution. Emission of dense smoke, noxious fumes, or fly ash.
10.Â Â Â Weeds, Brush. Dense growth of all weeds, vines, brush, or other
vegetation in the City so as to constitute a health, safety, or fire hazard.
11.Â Â Â Cotton Bearing or Diseased Trees. Cotton-bearing cottonwood trees and all
other cotton-bearing poplar trees on private property; trees infected with
Dutch Elm disease or knowingly impacted or damaged by the emerald ash borer on
private property.
12.Â Â Â Snow and Ice Accumulations. Snow and ice accumulations on sidewalks not
removed within 24 hours after the precipitation has stopped.
13.Â Â Â Containers. Refrigerators and freezers which are not stored under a
roofed enclosure, and which have doors that latch, lock, or otherwise secure
the door in a closed position.
14.Â Â Â Water Service Deficiency. Any break or leak in the water service link
between the City water main and any house or other building, when the break or
leak results in the escape of such volume of water as to constitute a hazard to
street, sidewalk, or terrace construction or as to interfere with the normal
use thereof.
15.Â Â Â Stables. The keeping or stabling of horses, mules, or asses so as to
cause obnoxious odors, noise, hazard, annoyances, or danger because of
confinement.
16.Â Â Â Stagnant Water. The permitting of water to accumulate and stand until
stagnant or upon any privately owned lot.
17.Â Â Â Junk, Refuse, Garbage. The permitting of junk, refuse, garbage, or filth
to accumulate on any lot or parcel.
18.Â Â Â Graffiti. All real property defaced by graffiti vandalism which is
visible to public view.
19.Â Â Â Junk or Abandoned Vehicles. The keeping or storing of a junk vehicle or
salvage vehicle on public property or private property not in an enclosed area.
A junk or salvage vehicle is defined as having one or more of the following
characteristics:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Unlicensed. Any vehicle not licensed for the current year as provided
by law.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Broken glass. Any vehicle or part of a vehicle with a broken windshield
or any other broken glass.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Broken or loose parts. Any vehicle or part of a vehicle with a broken
or loose fender, door, bumper, hood, wheel, steering wheel, trunk top, or
tailpipe.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â Missing engine or wheels. Any vehicle which is lacking an engine or one
or more wheels or other structural parts which renders such vehicle totally
inoperable.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â Habitat for animals or insects. Any vehicle or part of a vehicle which
has become a habitat for rats, mice, or snakes or any other vermin or insects.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â Defective or obsolete condition. Any vehicle or part of a vehicle
which, because of its defective or obsolete condition, constitutes a threat to
the public health and safety.
Â Â Â G.Â Â Â Inoperable condition. Any vehicle that is not capable of moving in both
forward and reverse gears.
20.Â Â Â Dangerous or unsafe building or structure. A dangerous or unsafe building
or structure shall mean any structure or building meeting any or all of the
following conditions or defects provided that such conditions or defects exist
to the extent that the life, health, property, or safety of the public or its
occupants are endangered whenever:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Any portion or member or appurtenance thereof is likely to fail or to
become detached or dislodged or to collapse and thereby injure persons or
damage property.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Any portion thereof has wracked, warped, buckled, or settled to such an
extent that walls or other structural portions have materially less resistance
to winds or earthquakes than is required in the case of similar new
construction.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The building or structure or any portion thereof, because of
dilapidation, deterioration, or decay; faulty construction; the removal,
movement, or instability of any portion of the ground necessary for the purpose
of supporting such building; the deterioration, decay, or inadequacy of its
foundations; or any other cause is likely to partially or completely collapse.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â For any reason the building or structure or any portion thereof is
manifestly unsafe for the purpose for which it is being used.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â The exterior walls or other vertical structural members list, lean, or
buckle to such an extent that a plumb line passing through the center of
gravity does not fall inside the middle one-third of the base.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â The building or structure has been so damaged by fire, wind,
earthquake, or flood or has become so dilapidated or deteriorated as to become
an attractive nuisance to children or a harbor for vagrants, criminals, or
immoral persons or as to enable persons to resort thereto for the purpose of
committing unlawful or immoral acts.
Â Â Â G.Â Â Â A building or structure used or intended to be used for dwelling
purposes, because of inadequate maintenance, dilapidation, decay, damage,
faulty construction or arrangement, inadequate light, air, or sanitation
facilities or otherwise is determined by the health officer to be unsanitary,
unfit for human habitation, or in such a condition that is likely to cause
sickness or disease.
Â Â Â H.Â Â Â Any building or structure, because of obsolescence, dilapidated
condition, deterioration, damage, inadequate exits, lack of sufficient fire
resistive construction, faulty electric wiring, gas connections, or heating
apparatus or other cause is determined by the Fire Marshal to be a fire hazard.
Â Â Â I.Â Â Â Any portion of a building or structure remains on a site after the
demolition or destruction of the building or structure, or any building or
structure is abandoned for a period of in excess of six months so as to
constitute such building or portion thereof an attractive nuisance or hazard to
the public.
21.Â Â Â Dumpsters on Residential Properties. Dumpsters are allowed on residential
properties for no more than 30 consecutive days. Dumpsters shall not be placed
in the City right-of-way. Dumpsters may be placed in the driveway or the yard
of the property in which they are serving. If a dumpster is placed in the yard
the surrounding vegetation shall be maintained at less than eight inches per
City Code.
50.03Â Â Â OTHER CONDITIONS REGULATED.
The following chapters of this Code of Ordinances contain regulations
prohibiting or restricting other conditions that are deemed to be nuisances:
1.Â Â Â Grass, Weeds, Vines, and Brush (See
Chapter 52)
2.Â Â Â Storage and Disposal of Solid Waste (See
Chapter 105)
3.Â Â Â Dangerous Buildings (See
Chapter 145)
4.Â Â Â Trees (See
Chapter 151)
5.Â Â Â Construction Codes and Regulations (See
Chapter 155)
50.04Â Â Â NUISANCES PROHIBITED; AUTHORITY TO ABATE.
The creation or maintenance of a nuisance is prohibited, and a nuisance, public
or private, may be abated in the manner provided for in this chapter or State
law.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 657.3)
50.05Â Â Â RIGHT OF ENTRY FOR INSPECTION.
1.Â Â Â Right of Entry and Administrative Search Warrants. Whenever necessary to
make an inspection to enforce any ordinance or whenever there is reasonable
cause to believe there exists an ordinance violation in any building or upon
any premises or real estate within the jurisdiction of the City, a City
official, upon presentation of proper credentials, may enter the building or
premises at all reasonable times to inspect the same or to perform any duty
imposed upon the official by this Code of Ordinances. Except in emergency
situations or when consent of the owner and/or occupant to the inspection has
otherwise been obtained, the City official shall give the owner and/or
occupant, if they can be located after reasonable effort, 24-hoursâ€™ written
notice of the officialâ€™s intention to inspect.
2.Â Â Â Warrants. If consent to enter upon or inspect any building, structure, or
property is withheld by any person having the lawful right to exclude, the City
official having the duty to enter upon or conduct the inspection may apply to
the Stateâ€™s District Court in and for the County, pursuant to I.C.A. Â§808.14,
for an administrative search warrant. No owner, operator, or occupant or any
other person having charge, care, or control of any dwelling, unit, rooming
unit, structure, building, or premises shall fail or neglect, after
presentation of a search warrant, to permit entry therein by the municipal
officer, designee, or employee.
50.06Â Â Â NOTICE TO ABATE; CONTENTS; SERVICE.
1.Â Â Â Required. Whenever a City official finds that a nuisance exists, such
official shall cause to be served upon the property owner as shown by the
records of the County Auditor and any other party in possession of the property
a written notice to abate the nuisance within a reasonable time after notice.
If a junk or abandoned vehicle is part of the nuisance to be abated, the
registered owner of the vehicle must also be notified.
2.Â Â Â Contents of Notice to Abate. The notice to abate served under this
subchapter shall contain the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â A description of what constitutes the nuisance.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The location of the nuisance.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â A statement of the necessary act to abate the nuisance.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â A stated reasonable time within which to complete the abatement.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â A statement that if the nuisance is not abated as directed and no
request for hearing is made within the period prescribed for the abatement, the
City will abate the nuisance and assess the costs against the owner of the
property.
3.Â Â Â Service of Notice to Abate.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The notice to abate shall be served either by:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â Personal delivery;
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â Sending a copy of the notice by certified Unites States mail; or
Â Â Â Â Â Â (3)Â Â Â Posting the notice in a conspicuous place upon the premises where
the nuisance exists.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Service of the notice by personal delivery may be completed by any City
official.
50.07Â Â Â REQUEST FOR HEARING.
Any person ordered to abate a nuisance may have a hearing with the Council as
to whether a nuisance exists. A request for hearing must be made in writing and
delivered to the Clerk within the time stated in the notice, or it will be
conclusively presumed that a nuisance exists and it must be abated as ordered.
The hearing will be before the Council at a time and place fixed by the
Council. The finding of the Council shall be conclusive and, if a nuisance is
found to exist, it shall be ordered abated within a reasonable time under the
circumstances.
50.08Â Â Â ABATEMENT IN EMERGENCY.
1.Â Â Â If it is determined that an emergency exists because of the continuing
maintenance of a nuisance, the City may perform any action which would be
required under this chapter without prior notice.
2.Â Â Â A determination may be made as to whether a nuisance exists based on the
following criteria:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Inability to contact the property owner by normal efforts;
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The seriousness of the violation due to health hazards or physical
hazards to a private individual or to the public as determined by a City
official; and
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Frequency of violations of a property owner or a tenant when the
property owner or tenant has received more than two nuisance violation
notifications within one calendar year. This determination is in effect for one
calendar year beginning on the date of the most recent nuisance violation
notification.
50.09Â Â Â ABATEMENT BY THE CITY; COSTS.
1.Â Â Â General.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â If the person notified to abate a nuisance neglects or fails to abate
as directed, the City may perform the required action to abate, keeping an
accurate account of the expense incurred.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The itemized expense account shall be filed with the Clerk who shall
pay such expenses on behalf of the City.
2.Â Â Â Collection of Costs of Abatement. The Clerk shall mail a statement of the
total expense incurred to the property owner who has failed to abide by the
notice to abate a nuisance under this chapter. If the amount shown on the
statement has not been paid within 30 days, the costs of the abatement shall be
certified to the County Treasurer, and shall then be collected with and in the
same manner as general property taxes pursuant to I.C.A. Chapter 384.
50.10Â Â Â NUISANCE VEHICLES; REMOVAL, STORAGE, REDEMPTION, OR DISPOSAL.
When a vehicle on public or private property is found to be a nuisance, the
vehicle may be removed and stored upon the premises secured by the City for
such storage purposes. The vehicle shall remain so stored upon said property
for a period of 14 days. At the end of such time, the vehicle shall be disposed
of by the City unless previously claimed by the owner. The City shall charge a
reasonable fee for the handling and storage of the vehicle to an owner claiming
a vehicle.
50.11Â Â Â PENALTY.
1.Â Â Â In lieu of the foregoing abatement procedures, the City may elect to treat
an unabated nuisance as a violation of this chapter, punishable as provided in
Chapter 3.
2.Â Â Â In addition, the creation or maintenance of a nuisance is a municipal
infraction, as defined in
Chapter 3, and is punishable by a civil penalty of not more than $750.00 for
the first offense and not to exceed $1,000.00 for each repeat offense.
CHAPTER 52
GRASS, WEEDS, VINES, AND BRUSH
Â 
52.01 Purpose                                     52.05 Notice to Owners
52.02 Definitions                                 52.06 Appeals
52.03 Maintenance of Right-of-Way and Residential 52.07 Failure to Comply
Property
52.04 Exemptions
Â 
52.01Â Â Â PURPOSE.
The purpose of this chapter is to require owners of residential property to cut
their grass, weeds, vines, and brush when it exceeds eight inches in height.
52.02Â Â Â DEFINITIONS.
For use in this chapter, the following terms are defined:
1.Â Â Â â€œResidential propertyâ€ means a property located in an area occupied by
residential dwellings including, but not limited to, houses and apartments and
any property within 200 feet of said dwelling.
2.Â Â Â â€œRight-of-Wayâ€ means the property outside a property ownerâ€™s lot and
property lines and inside the curb lines upon the public streets or, in the
absence of a curb, from the traveled portion of the public streets to the lot
or property.
52.03Â Â Â MAINTENANCE OF RIGHT-OF-WAY AND RESIDENTIAL PROPERTY.
All owners of residential property shall maintain their property and the
abutting right-of-way by cutting or destroying all grasses, weeds, vines, and
brush when said growth exceeds eight inches in height.
52.04Â Â Â EXEMPTIONS.
The following areas are exempt from the requirements of Section
52.03:
1.Â Â Â Property parcel that is 10 acres or larger.
2.Â Â Â Agricultural land.
3.Â Â Â Garden plants, orchards, vineyards, or farm crops.
4.Â Â Â Arboretums, recognized areas for the growth of native grass, flower
prairie, prairie grass or similar growth provided that the owner has been
granted an exemption by resolution of the Council, maintains the area free of
weeds and there is no safety, health, or fire hazard created by permitting said
growth.
5.Â Â Â Hillsides exceeding a two to one slope unless the growth creates a public
health or safety hazard
52.05Â Â Â NOTICE TO OWNERS.
The Clerk shall notify the property owner that a condition that violates the
terms of this chapter exists and shall notify the property owner of the actions
that must be performed to correct the condition. The notice shall state that
the condition shall be corrected within five days from the date that the notice
is issued.
52.06Â Â Â APPEALS.
If the property owner objects to the notice of action required under this
chapter, the objection shall be filed by the property owner with the Clerk in
writing within five days of the date of the notice. The objection shall be
heard by the Council without unnecessary delay and the Council shall make a
decision in writing. Failure to appeal within the time specified constitutes a
waiver of all rights to a hearing.
52.07Â Â Â FAILURE TO COMPLY.
If the property owner fails to maintain the property as required under this
chapter after notice is given as provided in this chapter, the work shall be
completed by City employees or a private contractor of the Cityâ€™s choosing. The
total cost of the expense of the work done, including any administrative fees,
shall be paid by the property owner. Failure to pay shall result in the cost
being assessed against the property for collection in the same manner as a
property tax.

(Code of Iowa, Sec. 717E.1)

5.Â Â Â â€œBusinessâ€ means any enterprise relating to any of the following:

Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The sale or offer for sale of goods or services.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A recruitment for employment or membership in an organization.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â A solicitation to make an investment.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â An amusement or entertainment activity.
6.Â Â Â â€œChickenâ€ means a domestic fowl, Gallus domesticus, developed in a number

7.Â Â Â â€œCommercial establishmentâ€ means an animal shelter, boarding kennel,

Â Â Â B.Â Â Â An exhibition of agricultural or manufactured products.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â An event for operation of amusement rides or devices or concession
booths.
9.Â Â Â â€œGameâ€ means a â€œgame of chanceâ€ or â€œgame of skillâ€ as defined in Section
99B.1 of the Code of Iowa.

10.Â Â Â â€œInjuryâ€ means an animalâ€™s disfigurement; the impairment of an animalâ€™s

55.02Â Â Â ANIMAL NEGLECT.
1.Â Â Â It is unlawful for a person who owns or has custody of an animal and
confines that animal to fail to provide the animal with any of the following
conditions for the animalâ€™s welfare:
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 717B.3)
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Access to food in an amount and quality reasonably sufficient to
satisfy the animalâ€™s basic nutrition level to the extent that the animalâ€™s
health or life is endangered.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Access to a supply of potable water in an amount reasonably sufficient
to satisfy the animalâ€™s basic hydration level to the extent that the animalâ€™s
health or life is endangered.Â Â Access to snow or ice does not satisfy this
requirement.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Sanitary conditions free from excessive animal waste or the
overcrowding of animals to the extent that the animalâ€™s health or life is
endangered.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â Ventilated shelter reasonably sufficient to provide adequate protection
from the elements and weather conditions suitable for the age, species, and
physical condition of the animal so as to maintain the animal in a state of
good health to the extent that the animalâ€™s health or life is endangered. The
shelter must protect the animal from wind, rain, snow, or sun and have adequate
bedding to provide reasonable protection against cold and dampness. A shelter
may include a residence, garage, barn, shed, or doghouse.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â Grooming, to the extent it is reasonably necessary to prevent adverse
health effects or suffering.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â Veterinary care deemed necessary by a reasonably prudent person to
relieve an animalâ€™s distress from any of the following:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â A condition caused by failing to provide for the animalâ€™s welfare
as described in this section.
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â An injury or illness suffered by the animal causing the animal to
suffer prolonged pain and suffering.
2.Â Â Â This section does not apply to any of the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â A person operating a commercial establishment under a valid
authorization issued or renewed under Section 162.2A of the Code of Iowa, or a
person acting under the direction or supervision of that person, if all of the
following apply:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â The animal, as described in Subsection 1, was maintained as part of
the commercial establishmentâ€™s operation.
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â In providing conditions for the welfare of the animal, as described
in Subsection 1, the person complied with the standard of care requirements
provided in Section 162.10A[1] of the Code of Iowa, including any applicable
rules adopted by the Department of Agriculture and Land Stewardship applying
to: (i) a State licensee or registrant operating pursuant to Section 162.10A
[2a] or [2b] of the Code of Iowa; or (ii) a permittee operating pursuant to
Section 162.10A[2c] of the Code of Iowa.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â AÂ research facility if the research facilityÂ has been issued or renewed
a valid authorization by the Department of Agriculture and Land Stewardship
pursuant to Chapter 162Â of the Code of Iowa, and performs functions within the
scope of accepted practices and disciplines associated with the research
facility.
55.03Â Â Â LIVESTOCK NEGLECT.
It is unlawful for a person who impounds or confines livestock in any place to
fail to provide the livestock with care consistent with customary animal
husbandry practices, or to deprive the livestock of necessary sustenance, or to
injure or destroy livestock by any means that causes pain or suffering in a
manner inconsistent with customary animal husbandry practices.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 717.2)
55.04Â Â Â ABANDONMENT OF CATS AND DOGS.
It is unlawful for a person who owns or has custody of a cat or dog to
relinquish all rights in and duties to care for the cat or dog. This section
does not apply to any of the following:
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 717B.8)
1.Â Â Â The delivery of aÂ cat or dog to another person who will accept ownership
and custody of theÂ cat or dog.
2.Â Â Â The delivery of aÂ cat or dog to an animal shelter or that has been issued
or renewed a valid authorization by the Department of Agriculture and Land
Stewardship under Chapter 162 of the Code of Iowa.
3.Â Â Â A person who relinquishes custody of a cat at a location in which the
person does not hold a legal or equitable interest, if previously the person
had taken custody of the cat at the same location and provided for the catâ€™s
sterilization by a veterinarian.
55.05Â Â Â LIVESTOCK.
It is unlawful for a person to keep livestock within the City except by written
consent of the Council or except as permitted in the A-1 Agricultural Zoning
District. Notwithstanding the provisions of this section, the keeping of
domestic chickens shall be permitted in residential zoning districts so long as
such keeping is in compliance with this subsection and all other applicable
City ordinances unless, despite compliance with the following, the presence of
such chickens is still likely to endanger the health, safety, peace, quiet,
comfort, enjoyment of, or otherwise become a public nuisance to nearby
residents or occupants or places of business:
1.Â Â Â Chickens must be confined in a coop or fowl house not less than 18 inches
in height or, in the alternative, within a fenced pen area. Chickens must be
kept within the coop, the fowl house, or the fenced pen area at all times.
2.Â Â Â The coop, the fowl house, or the fenced pen area must be of such a design
to be reasonably expected to prevent entry by dogs, cats, or other animals and
shall be completely enclosed.
3.Â Â Â The coop or fowl house must be used for chickens only and must be well
ventilated.
4.Â Â Â The coop, the fowl house, or the fenced pen area shall have a minimum of
four square feet of floor area for each chicken but shall not be any larger
than 12 square feet of area for each chicken. The coop, fowl house, or fenced
pen area shall be a minimum of 25 feet from any property line.
5.Â Â Â Any coop, fowl house, or fenced pen area must be well drained so there is
no accumulation of moisture.
6.Â Â Â Any coop, fowl house, or fenced pen area shall be kept clean, sanitary,
and free from accumulation of chicken excrement and objectionable odors. It
shall be cleaned daily, and all droppings and body excretions shall be either
placed in fly-proof containers and double- bagged in plastic bags or, in the
alternative, used as fertilizer on the same property or, with the ownerâ€™s
permission, on other property so long as the droppings and body excretions are
spread and incorporated into the soil within 24 hours or otherwise disposed of
lawfully.
7.Â Â Â All chicken feed shall be stored in rodent-proof containers.
8.Â Â Â No more than six chickens shall be kept or maintained per property.
9.Â Â Â All such chickens must be hens; no roosters are permitted.
10.Â Â Â The City shall not be liable for injury or death of chickens caused by
dogs, cats, or other animals, domestic or wild, whether such animals are
licensed by the City or not. Further, injury or death of a chicken caused by an
animal is not, in and of itself, sufficient grounds for the City to determine
that the animal is a vicious animal pursuant to
Chapter 56 of this Code of Ordinances.
11.Â Â Â Any slaughter of chickens not regulated by State law or otherwise
forbidden or regulated shall be done only in a humane and sanitary manner and
shall not be done open to the view of any public area or adjacent property
owned by another.
12.Â Â Â An owner or possessor of animals on property that is newly annexed and in
a zoning district other than A-1 Agricultural District has 90 days from the
date of annexation to bring the property into compliance required by this
section.
13.Â Â Â A violation of this subsection is a municipal infraction as provided in
Chapter 3.
55.06Â Â Â AT LARGE PROHIBITED.
It is unlawful for any owner to allow an animal to run at large within the
corporate limits of the City. Any dog, while on a street, sidewalk, public way
or in any park, public square, or other public space, or upon any private
property without the consent of the owner, shall be secured by a leash or chain
of sufficient tensile strength to restrain the particular dog, or shall be at
heel and securely muzzled.
(Section 55.06 â€“ Ord. 74-2024 â€“ Jun. 24 Supp.)
55.07Â Â Â DAMAGE OR INTERFERENCE.
It is unlawful for the owner of an animal to allow or permit such animal to
pass upon the premises of another thereby causing damage to, or interference
with, the premises.
55.08Â Â Â ANNOYANCE OR DISTURBANCE.
It is unlawful for the owner of a dog to allow or permit such dog to cause
serious annoyance or disturbance to any person by frequent and habitual
howling, yelping, barking, or otherwise, or by running after or chasing
persons, bicycles, automobiles, or other vehicles.
55.09Â Â Â RABIES VACCINATION.
Every owner of a dog shall obtain a rabies vaccination for such animal. It is
unlawful for any person to own or have a dog in said personâ€™s possession, six
months of age or over, which has not been vaccinated against rabies. Dogs kept
in State or federally licensed kennels and not allowed to run at large are not
subject to these vaccination requirements.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.33)
55.10Â Â Â OWNERâ€™S DUTY.
It is the duty of the owner of any dog, cat, or other animal that has bitten or
attacked a person or any person having knowledge of such bite or attack to
report this act to a local health or law enforcement official. It is the duty
of physicians and veterinarians to report to the local board of health the
existence of any animal known or suspected to be suffering from rabies.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.38)
55.11Â Â Â CONFINEMENT.
If a local board of health receives information that an animal has bitten a
person or that a dog or animal is suspected of having rabies, the board shall
order the owner to confine such animal in the manner it directs. If the owner
fails to confine such animal in the manner directed, the animal shall be
apprehended and impounded by such board, and after 10 days the board may
humanely destroy the animal. If such animal is returned to its owner, the owner
shall pay the cost of impoundment. This section does not apply if a police
service dog or a horse used by a law enforcement agency and acting in the
performance of its duties has bitten a person.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.39)
55.12Â Â Â AT LARGE: IMPOUNDMENT.
1.Â Â Â In addition to any other remedies provided in this chapter, a law
enforcement or other City official may seize, impound and humanely confine to
an animal shelter or hospital any of the following animals:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Any animal at large;
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Any animal constituting a public nuisance or considered a danger to the
public;
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Any animal that is in violation of any quarantine or confinement order
of the County health official or Cedar Valley Humane Society;
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â Any unattended animal that is ill, injured, or otherwise in need of
care;
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â Any animal that is reasonably believed to have been abused or
neglected;
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â Any animal that is reasonably suspected of having rabies;
Â Â Â G.Â Â Â Any animal that is charged with being a dangerous or vicious animal
pursuant to Chapter 56 and a law enforcement officer or the Council determines
that there is a threat to public health and safety;
Â Â Â H.Â Â Â Any animal that a court of competent jurisdiction has ordered
impounded, destroyed, or removed from the City limits;
Â Â Â I.Â Â Â Any animal that is considered unattended or abandoned, as in situations
where the owner is deceased, has been arrested or evicted from their regular
place of residence.
Any law enforcement or City official may also, or in lieu of impoundment, issue
to the owner a notice of violation.
2.Â Â Â Private Capture of Animals at Large. Any person finding an animal at large
upon their private property may remove the animal to any animal shelter that
will take possession of the animal. If no such shelter is available, the person
may hold the animal in his or her own possession, and as soon as possible,
notify the Mayor or Clerk. The property owner shall provide a description of
the animal and the name of the owner if known. The Mayor shall dispatch an
authorized representative to take possession of the animal.
55.13Â Â Â DISPOSITION OF ANIMALS.
When an animal has been apprehended and impounded, written notice shall be
provided to the owner within two days after impoundment, if the ownerâ€™s name
and current address can reasonably be determined by accessing a tag or other
device that is on or part of the animal. Impounded animals may be redeemed by
the owner upon payment of impounding costs, and if an unvaccinated dog or cat,
by having it immediately vaccinated pursuant to Section
55.19 and payment of the associated costs. If the owner fails to redeem the
animal within seven days from the date that the notice is mailed, or if the
owner cannot be located within seven days, the animal shall be disposed of in
accordance with law or destroyed by euthanasia.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.37, 351.41)
55.14Â Â Â IMPOUNDING COSTS.
Impounding costs are set by resolution of the Council.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.37)
55.15Â Â Â PET AWARDS PROHIBITED.
(Code of Iowa, Ch. 717E)
1.Â Â Â Prohibition. It is unlawful for any person to award a pet or advertise
that a pet may be awarded as any of the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â A prize for participating in a game.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A prize for participating in a fair.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â An inducement or condition for visiting a place of business or
attending an event sponsored by a business.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â An inducement or condition for executing a contract that includes
provisions unrelated to the ownership, care, or disposition of the pet.
2.Â Â Â Exceptions. This section does not apply to any of the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â A pet shop licensed pursuant to Section 162.5 of the Code of Iowa if
the award of a pet is provided in connection with the sale of a pet on the
premises of the pet shop.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Youth programs associated with 4-H Clubs; Future Farmers of America;
the Izaak Walton League of America; or organizations associated with outdoor
recreation, hunting, or fishing, including but not limited to the Iowa
Sportsmenâ€™s Federation.
55.16Â Â Â TRAPPING.
No person shall trap game or fur-bearing animals by use of leg hold or snare
traps within the City limits.
55.17Â Â Â KEEPING OF NUMEROUS ANIMALS LIMITED.
Except with advanced permission of the Council, no person shall own, harbor, or
keep more than a combined total of five dogs or five cats, or a mixture of five
such animals over the age of four months. This limit shall not apply to an
appropriate licensed kennel, sanctuary, veterinary officer, or similar business
that provides boarding or veterinary care for such animals in properly zoned
commercial districts.
55.18Â Â Â SANITATION.
1.Â Â Â No owner or custodian of any animal shall cause or allow such animal to
soil, defile or defecate on any public property or upon any street, sidewalk,
public way, play area or common grounds owned jointly by the members of a
homeowners or condominium association, or upon private property other than that
of the owner, unless such owner or custodian immediately removes and disposes
of all feces deposited by such animal by the following methods:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Collection of the feces by appropriate implement and placement in a
paper or plastic bag or other container; and
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Removal of such bag or container to the property of the animal owner or
custodian and disposition thereafter in a manner as permitted by law.
2.Â Â Â No person owning, harboring, or keeping an animal within the City shall
permit any waste matter from the animal to collect and remain on the property
of the owner or custodian, or on the property of others so as to cause or
create an unhealthy, unsanitary, dangerous, or offensive living condition on
the ownerâ€™s or custodianâ€™s property, or to abutting property of others.
3.Â Â Â No person owning, harboring, keeping, or in charge of any animal shall
cause unsanitary dangerous or offensive conditions by virtue of the size or
number of animals maintained at a single location or due to the inadequacy of
the facilities.
55.19Â Â Â LICENSING OF DOGS AND CATS.
1.Â Â Â It is unlawful for any person to own, keep, or harbor a cat or dog over
four months of age which has not been currently vaccinated against rabies in
accordance with the Compendium of Animals Rabies Control as compiled by the
National Association of State Public Health Veterinarians. Dogs kept in State
or federally licensed kennels and not allowed to run at large are not subject
to these vaccination requirements.
2.Â Â Â Every cat or dog which is over four months of age shall wear a collar with
a valid rabies vaccination tag attached to the collar when outside the ownerâ€™s
dwelling.
3.Â Â Â Cats and dogs shall be licensed by their owners through the procedure by
which the rabies vaccination tag and certificate are obtained. The rabies
vaccination tag and certificate shall be the license required by this chapter.
4.Â Â Â The owner of any dog or cat within the City which is subject to
vaccination in accordance with the provisions of this chapter shall have such
dog or cat vaccinated against rabies by a licensed veterinarian in such way as
to maintain said dog or catâ€™s immunity from rabies.
5.Â Â Â The owner shall attach a permanent identification device to the cat or
dogâ€™s collar which contains the address and/or telephone number of the cat or
dogâ€™s owner or veterinarian unless the information is engraved on the rabies
vaccination tag. The owner shall notify the veterinarian who vaccinated the cat
or dog for rabies of any change of address within five days of moving. When
permanent ownership of a cat or dog is transferred, the original owner must
notify the veterinarian who vaccinated said cat or dog for rabies of the
transfer and provide the new ownerâ€™s name, address, and telephone number within
five days after the transfer.
55.20Â Â Â TAMPERING WITH A RABIES VACCINATION TAG.
It is unlawful to tamper with a rabies vaccination tag.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.45)
1.Â Â Â A person commits the offense of tampering with a rabies vaccination tag if
all of the following apply:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The person knowingly removes, damages, or destroys a rabies vaccination
tag as described in Section 351.35 of the Code of Iowa.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The rabies vaccination tag is attached to a collar worn by a dog,
including as provided in Sections 351.25 and 351.26 of the Code of Iowa.
2.Â Â Â This section shall not apply to an act taken by any of the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The owner of the dog, an agent of the owner, or a person authorized to
take action by the owner.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A peace officer.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â A veterinarian.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â An animal shelter or pound.
55.21Â Â Â TAMPERING WITH AN ELECTRONIC HANDLING DEVICE.
It is unlawful to tamper with an electronic handling device.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 351.46)
1.Â Â Â A person commits the offense of tampering with an electronic handling
device if all of the following apply:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The person knowingly removes, disables, or destroys an electronic
device designed and used to maintain custody or control of the dog or modify
the dogâ€™s behavior.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The electronic device is attached to or worn by the dog or attached to
an item worn by the dog, including (but not limited to) a collar, harness, or
vest.
2.Â Â Â This section shall not apply to an act taken by any of the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The owner of the dog, an agent of the owner, or a person authorized to
take action by the owner.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A peace officer.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â A veterinarian.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â An animal shelter or pound.
CHAPTER 57
DANGEROUS AND VICIOUS ANIMALS
Â 
57.01 Definitions                  57.03 Keeping of Vicious Animals Prohibited
57.02 Keeping of Dangerous Animals 57.04 Seizure, Impoundment, and Disposition
Prohibited
Â 
57.01Â Â Â DEFINITIONS.
For use in this chapter, the following terms are defined:
1.Â Â Â â€œDangerous animalâ€ means:  â€ 
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Badgers, wolverines, weasels, skunk, and mink.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Raccoons.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Bats.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â Scorpions.
2.Â Â Â â€œVicious animalâ€ means any of the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Any animal, except for a dangerous animal as listed above, that has
attacked, bitten, or clawed a person while running at large and the attack was
unprovoked; or,
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Any animal, except for a dangerous animal as listed above, that has
exhibited vicious tendencies in present or past conduct, including such that
said animal:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â Has attacked, bitten, or clawed a person causing injury; or,
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â Has bitten more than one person during the animalâ€™s lifetime; or,
Â Â Â Â Â Â (3)Â Â Â Has bitten one person on two or more occasions during the animalâ€™s
lifetime; or,
Â Â Â Â Â Â (4)Â Â Â Has attacked any domestic animal or fowl without provocation,
causing injury or death while off the property of the owner.
Â 
Notes
  â€ Â EDITORâ€™S NOTE: Certain other dangerous animals, listed in Chapter 717F.1,
â€Paragraph 5a, of the Code of Iowa, are specifically prohibited and regulated by
  the Iowa Department of Agriculture and Land Stewardship.
57.02Â Â Â KEEPING OF DANGEROUS ANIMALS PROHIBITED.
No person shall keep, shelter, or harbor any dangerous animal as a pet, or act
as a temporary custodian for such animal, or keep, shelter, or harbor such
animal for any purpose or in any capacity within the City.
57.03Â Â Â KEEPING OF VICIOUS ANIMALS PROHIBITED.
No person shall keep, shelter, or harbor for any reason within the City a
vicious animal except in the following circumstances:
1.Â Â Â Animals under the control of a law enforcement or military agency.
2.Â Â Â The keeping of guard dogs; however, guard dogs must be kept within a
structure or fixed enclosure at all times, and any guard dog found at large may
be processed as a vicious animal pursuant to the provisions of this chapter.
Any premises guarded by a guard dog shall be prominently posted with a sign
containing the wording â€œGuard Dog,â€ â€œVicious Dogâ€ or words of similar import,
and the owner of such premises shall inform the Mayor or peace officer that a
guard dog is on duty at said premises.
57.04Â Â Â SEIZURE, IMPOUNDMENT, AND DISPOSITION.
1.Â Â Â In the event that a dangerous animal or vicious animal is found at large
and unattended upon public property, park property, public right-of-way or the
property of someone other than its owner, thereby creating a hazard to persons
or property, such animal may, in the discretion of the Mayor or peace officer,
be destroyed if it cannot be confined or captured. The City shall be under no
duty to attempt the confinement or capture of a dangerous animal or vicious
animal found at large, nor shall it have a duty to notify the owner of such
animal prior to its destruction.
2.Â Â Â Upon the complaint of any individual that a person is keeping, sheltering
or harboring a dangerous animal or vicious animal on premises in the City, the
Mayor or peace officer shall cause the matter to be investigated and if after
investigation, the facts indicate that the person named in the complaint is
keeping, sheltering or harboring a dangerous or vicious animal in the City, the
Mayor or peace officer shall order the person named in the complaint to safely
remove such animal from the City or destroy the animal within three days of the
receipt of such an order. Such order shall be contained in a notice to remove
the dangerous or vicious animal, which notice shall be given in writing to the
person keeping, sheltering, or harboring the dangerous animal or vicious
animal, and shall be served personally or by certified mail. Such order and
notice to remove the dangerous animal or vicious animal shall not be required
where such animal has previously caused serious physical harm or death to any
person, in which case the Mayor or peace officer shall cause the animal to be
immediately seized and impounded or killed if seizure and impoundment are not
possible without risk of serious physical harm or death to any person.
3.Â Â Â The order to remove a dangerous animal or vicious animal issued by the
Mayor or peace officer may be appealed to the Council. In order to appeal such
order, written notice of appeal must be filed with the Clerk within three days
after receipt of the order contained in the notice to remove the dangerous or
vicious animal. Failure to file such written notice of appeal shall constitute
a waiver of the right to appeal the order of the Mayor or peace officer.
4.Â Â Â The notice of appeal shall state the grounds for such appeal and shall be
delivered personally or by certified mail to the Clerk. The hearing of such
appeal shall be scheduled within seven days of the receipt of the notice of
appeal. The hearing may be continued for good cause. After such hearing, the
Council may affirm or reverse the order of the Mayor or peace officer. Such
determination shall be contained in a written decision and shall be filed with
the Clerk within three days after the hearing or any continued session thereof.
5.Â Â Â If the Council affirms the action of the Mayor or peace officer, the
Council shall order in its written decision that the person owning, sheltering,
harboring, or keeping such dangerous or vicious animal remove such animal from
the City or destroy it. The decision and order shall immediately be served upon
the person against whom rendered in the same manner as the notice of removal.
If the original order of the Mayor or peace officer is not appealed and is not
complied with within three days or the order of the Council after appeal is not
complied with within three days of its issuance, the Mayor or peace officer is
authorized to seize, impound, or destroy such dangerous or vicious animal.
Failure to comply with an order of the Mayor or peace officer issued pursuant
to this chapter and not appealed (or of the Council after appeal) constitutes a
simple misdemeanor.
CHAPTER 58
PUBLIC HEALTH NUISANCE REGULATIONS AND ENFORCEMENT PROCEDURES
Â 
58.01 Purpose                                 58.05 Investigation and Procedure
58.02 International Property Maintenance Code 58.06 Enforcement
Adopted
58.03 Public Health Nuisances Enumerated      58.07 Penalty
58.04 Health Officer
Â 
58.01Â Â Â PURPOSE.
The purpose of this chapter is to provide minimum standards for the protection
and safeguard of life and limb, health, property, and the general public
welfare by controlling health nuisances in the City.
58.02Â Â Â INTERNATIONAL PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE ADOPTED.
The International Property Maintenance Code as adopted and modified by Linn
County in Chapter 105, Article VI, or its successor provisions, of the County
Code of Ordinances is hereby adopted and incorporated into this Code of
Ordinances by this reference.
58.03Â Â Â PUBLIC HEALTH NUISANCES ENUMERATED.
The following are deemed to be public health nuisances within the City:
1.Â Â Â The accumulation of garbage, refuse, junk, or rubbish so as to constitute
a public health threat.
2.Â Â Â The presence of two or more inoperable vehicles, regardless of whether
such vehicles are licensed.
3.Â Â Â The presence of any vehicle found to harbor vermin or contaminate the
environment so as to present a threat to public health.
4.Â Â Â The presence of vermin, insects, birds, or bats, or conditions that allow
for harboring vermin, insects, birds, or bats, so as to present a threat to
public health.
5.Â Â Â The storage or discharge of rubbish, flammable refuse, liquid, or other
material in any building or on any place in such a manner as to constitute a
hazard of fire injury to the occupant, individuals, or the public.
6.Â Â Â Habitation in a structure without sanitary facilities.
7.Â Â Â Habitation in a structure without adequate water supply.
8.Â Â Â Any structure that is vacant and unfit for human habitation and occupancy,
but not in danger of structural collapse.
9.Â Â Â Any swimming pool that has not been maintained so as to prevent the growth
of organisms or the development of insect eggs or larvae for 30 or more
consecutive days.
10.Â Â Â Any swimming pool that is empty, not filled to the grade of adjacent
land, and not kept free of standing water or debris for 30 or more consecutive
days.
11.Â Â Â Habitation in any structure without heating facilities capable of
maintaining a room temperature of at least 68 degrees Fahrenheit.
12.Â Â Â Any structure or equipment found by the Health Officer to be dangerous,
unsafe, unlawful, unsanitary, or unfit for human occupancy under the policies
of the County Health Department.
58.04Â Â Â HEALTH OFFICER.
The Council shall designate a person or agency as the Health Officer for the
City.
58.05Â Â Â INVESTIGATION AND PROCEDURE.
The Health Officer shall have the right, upon presentation of proper
credentials, to request entry into or upon any property or premises, public or
private, in the City at any reasonable hour for the purpose of investigating
and documenting any complaint or alleged violation of this chapter. Such
investigation and documentation shall be conducted according to the policies
and procedures related to public health nuisances adopted by the County Board
of Health.
58.06Â Â Â ENFORCEMENT.
Enforcement of this chapter shall be according to the provisions of Sections
50.06-
50.11 of this Code of Ordinances.
58.07Â Â Â PENALTY.
Any violation of this chapter shall be a municipal infraction enforceable under
Chapter 3 of this Code of Ordinances.
CHAPTER 60

60.01Â Â Â TITLE.
Chapters
60 through
70 of this Code of Ordinances may be known and cited as the â€œPalo Traffic Codeâ€
(and are referred to herein as the â€œTraffic Codeâ€).
60.02Â Â Â DEFINITIONS.
Where words and phrases used in the Traffic Code are defined by State law, such
definitions apply to their use in said Traffic Code and are adopted by
reference. Those definitions so adopted that need further definition or are
reiterated, and other words and phrases used herein, have the following
meanings:
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.1)
1.Â Â Â â€œBusiness Districtâ€ means the territory contiguous to and including a
highway when 50 percent or more of the frontage thereon for a distance of 300
feet or more is occupied by buildings in use for business.
2.Â Â Â â€œMPHâ€ means miles per hour.
3.Â Â Â â€œParadeâ€ means any march or procession of persons or vehicles organized
for marching or moving on the streets in an organized fashion or manner or any
march or procession of persons or vehicles represented or advertised to the
public as a parade.
4.Â Â Â â€œParkâ€ or â€œparkingâ€ means the standing of a vehicle, whether occupied or
not, otherwise than temporarily for the purpose of and while actually engaged
in loading or unloading merchandise or passengers.
5.Â Â Â â€œPeace officerâ€ means every officer, not limited to Sheriff, Deputies, and
other law enforcement officers, authorized to direct or regulate traffic or to
make arrests for violations of traffic regulations.
6.Â Â Â â€œResidence districtâ€ means the territory contiguous to and including a
highway not comprising a business, suburban, or school district, where 40
percent or more of the frontage on such a highway for a distance of 300 feet or
more is occupied by dwellings or by dwellings and buildings in use for
business.
7.Â Â Â â€œSchool districtâ€ means the territory contiguous to and including a
highway for a distance of 200 feet in either direction from a schoolhouse.
8.Â Â Â â€œStandâ€ or â€œstandingâ€ means the halting of a vehicle, whether occupied or
not, otherwise than for the purpose of and while actually engaged in receiving
or discharging passengers.
9.Â Â Â â€œStopâ€ means when required, the complete cessation of movement.
10.Â Â Â â€œStopâ€ or â€œstoppingâ€ means when prohibited, any halting of a vehicle,
even momentarily, whether occupied or not, except when necessary to avoid
conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the directions of a peace
officer or traffic control sign or signal.
11.Â Â Â â€œSuburban districtâ€ means all other parts of the City not included in the
business, school, or residence districts.
12.Â Â Â â€œTraffic control deviceâ€ means all signs, signals, markings, and devices
not inconsistent with this chapter, lawfully placed or erected for the purpose
of regulating, warning, or guiding traffic.
13.Â Â Â â€œVehicleâ€ means every device in, upon, or by which any person or property
is or may be transported or drawn upon a public highway, street, or alley.
60.03Â Â Â ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT.
Provisions of this Traffic Code and State law relating to motor vehicles and
law of the road are enforced by the Linn County Sheriffâ€™s Department.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 372.13[4])
60.04Â Â Â POWER TO DIRECT TRAFFIC.
A peace officer or, in the absence of a peace officer, any officer of the Fire
Department when at the scene of a fire, is authorized to direct all traffic by
voice, hand, or signal in conformance with traffic laws. In the event of an
emergency, traffic may be directed as conditions require, notwithstanding the
provisions of the traffic laws.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 102.4 and 321.236[2])
60.05Â Â Â REPORTS OF TRAFFIC ACCIDENTS.
The driver of a vehicle involved in an accident within the limits of the City
shall file a report as and when required by the Iowa Department of
Transportation. A copy of this report shall be filed with the Linn County
Sheriffâ€™s Department for the confidential use of peace officers and shall be
subject to the provisions of Section 321.271 of the Code of Iowa.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.273)
60.06Â Â Â PEACE OFFICERâ€™S AUTHORITY.
A peace officer is authorized to stop a vehicle to require exhibition of the
driverâ€™s license of the driver, to serve a summons or memorandum of traffic
violation, to inspect the condition of the vehicle, to inspect the vehicle with
reference to size, weight, cargo, log book, bills of lading, or other manifest
of employment, tires and safety equipment, or to inspect the registration
certificate, the compensation certificate, travel order, or permit of such
vehicle. A peace officer having probable cause to stop a vehicle may require
exhibition of the proof of financial liability coverage card issued for the
vehicle.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.492)
60.07Â Â Â OBEDIENCE TO PEACE OFFICERS.
No person shall willfully fail or refuse to comply with any lawful order or
direction of any peace officer invested by law with authority to direct,
control, or regulate traffic.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.229)
60.08Â Â Â PARADES REGULATED.
No person shall conduct or cause any parade on any street except as provided
herein:
1.Â Â Â Approval Required. No parade shall be conducted without first obtaining
approval from the Council. The person organizing or sponsoring the parade shall
provide information concerning the time and date for the parade and the streets
or general route therefor, and any approval given to such person includes all
participants in the parade, provided they have been invited to participate.
2.Â Â Â Parade Not a Street Obstruction. Any parade for which approval has been
given and the persons lawfully participating therein shall not be deemed an
obstruction of the streets, notwithstanding the provisions of any other
ordinance to the contrary.
3.Â Â Â Control by Peace Officers and Firefighters. Persons participating in any
parade shall at all times be subject to the lawful orders and directions in the
performance of their duties of law enforcement personnel and members of the
Fire Department.
CHAPTER 61
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES
Â 
61.01 Installation  61.04 Standards
61.02 Crosswalks    61.05 Compliance
61.03 Traffic Lanes
Â 
61.01Â Â Â INSTALLATION.
The Council shall establish by resolution, and cause to be placed and
maintained, appropriate traffic control devices to indicate parking spaces and
zones, no parking zones, limited parking zones, reserved parking zones, loading
zones, safety zones, school zones, hospital zones, quiet zones, traffic zones
other than the above, truck routes, school stops, stop intersections, yield
right-of-way intersections, one-way streets, streets to be laned for traffic,
and play streets. The Council shall also have the power to designate and
indicate by resolution intersections at which traffic shall be controlled by
traffic signals; intersections at which left turns, right turns and U-turns
shall be prohibited; and intersections at which markers, buttons or other
indications shall be placed to indicate the course to be traveled by vehicles
traversing or turning at such intersections. The City shall keep a record of
all such traffic control devices.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.254 and 321.255)
61.02Â Â Â CROSSWALKS.
The Council is hereby authorized to designate and maintain crosswalks by
appropriate traffic control devices at intersections where, due to traffic
conditions, there is particular danger to pedestrians crossing the street or
roadway, and at such other places as traffic conditions require.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 372.13[4] and 321.255)
61.03Â Â Â TRAFFIC LANES.
The Council is hereby authorized to mark lanes for traffic on street pavements
at such places as traffic conditions require, consistent with this Traffic
Code. Where such traffic lanes have been marked, it is unlawful for the
operator of any vehicle to fail or refuse to keep such vehicle within the
boundaries of any such lane except when lawfully passing another vehicle or
preparatory to making a lawful turning movement.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 372.13[4] and 321.255)
61.04Â Â Â STANDARDS.
Traffic control devices shall comply with standards established by The Manual
of Uniform Traffic Control Devices for Streets and Highways as supplemented by
State law or regulation.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.255)
61.05Â Â Â COMPLIANCE.
No driver of a vehicle shall disobey the instructions of any official traffic
control device placed in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, unless
at the time otherwise directed by a peace officer, subject to the exceptions
granted the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle under Sections 321.231
and 321.231A of the Code of Iowa.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 321.256)
