170.09Â Â Â IMPROVEMENTS REQUIRED.
The subdivider shall, at said subdividerâ€™s expense, install and construct all
improvements required by this chapter,
Chapter 161, and as shown on the preliminary plat within the subdivision
proper. All required improvements shall be constructed in accordance with the
aforementioned design standards established for such improvements as defined by
SUDAS and shall be reviewed by the City and the City Engineer.
1.Â Â Â Urban Renewal Area Exception. The City may consider waiving portions of
this section if all of the following circumstances exist:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The subdivision is located within an active urban renewal area eligible
for tax increment reimbursement, and;
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The subdivider can demonstrate how the Cityâ€™s participation in cost
sharing for improvements within the subdivision will achieve the goals and
objectives of the urban renewal area, and;
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The subdivider is prepared to offer the City an infrastructure
improvement, property, or service that is equal or commensurate to the Cityâ€™s
financial contribution and meets the stated goals and objectives of the Cityâ€™s
Urban Renewal Plan.
2.Â Â Â In some cases, there may be a need to extend municipal utilities and
services to the edge of a subdivision. The City will decide on a case-by-case
basis as to the financial responsibilities of the subdivider and the City
regarding these utility and service extensions
170.10Â Â Â INSPECTION.
1.Â Â Â Construction Observation. All improvements shall be inspected to ensure
compliance with the approved plans, technical specifications and details by the
City Engineer. It is the ultimate responsibility of the subdivider and his or
her professional engineer to provide assurance that the required improvements
are constructed in accordance with the approved plans, technical specifications
and details, and any specific standards contained in this Code. The cost of
such inspection shall be borne by the subdivider and shall be the actual cost
of the inspection to the City. Reimbursements for said costs shall be received
prior to Final Plat approval. No building permits or certificates of occupancy
shall be issued until all fees are paid in full. The subdivider shall provide
the City Engineer with a construction schedule prior to the commencement of any
and all construction and notify the City Engineer not less than 48 hours in
advance of readiness for required inspections.
2.Â Â Â Materials Testing. In addition, materials testing may be required by a
professional testing service as he or she may deem necessary to assure that the
public improvements meet the Design Standards and Specifications Manuals and
any specific standards contained in this Code or the laws of the State or the
United States. Materials testing shall be coordinated by the City Engineer and
paid for by the subdivider in the same manner that the inspections are paid for
above.
170.11Â Â Â MINIMUM IMPROVEMENTS.
The improvements set forth below shall be considered the minimum improvements
necessary to protect the public health, safety, and welfare. All of the minimum
improvements mandated by this section shall be designed and constructed in
accordance with the requirements of SUDAS. The subdivider must provide evidence
of any and all construction permits, highway or road easements and access, or
other appropriate documentation from State or federal regulatory agencies prior
to approval of the final plat. Easements from all utility companies will also
be required. The City reserves the right to request changes to a proposed
subdivision that may exceed the municipal capacities for streets, sewer, water,
or other services. In this event, the City may request a proportional fee from
the subdivider, to be determined by the City and the City Engineer, for any
required capacity improvements.
1.Â Â Â Streets; General. The subdivider of land being subdivided shall provide
the grading of the entire street right-of-way, alley, or public place and
provide appropriate paving.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Under some circumstances the City may require, as a condition for
approval of the plat, dedication and improvement of a street having a width
greater than necessary to meet the needs of the platted area, but necessary to
complete the City street system as it relates to both the area being platted
and other areas. In such event, the City may pay the subdivider the difference
in cost of improving the wider street and the street width reasonable to meet
the foreseeable needs of the subdivision taken alone. The streets shall, upon
final approval and acceptance by the City, become the property of the City.
2.Â Â Â Sanitary Sewer System; General. The subdivider of the land being platted
shall make adequate provision for the disposal of sanitary sewage from the
platted area with due regard being given to present or reasonably foreseeable
needs. There shall be constructed, at the subdividerâ€™s expense, a sanitary
sewer system including all necessary pumping stations, pumping equipment, sewer
access holes, and all other necessary or desirable appurtenances to provide for
the discharge of sanitary sewage from all lots or parcels of land within the
platted area to a connection with the Cityâ€™s sanitary sewer. The Cityâ€™s role in
reviewing the plans is to determine the sanitary sewerâ€™s placement, size, and
route.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Under some circumstances the City may require, as a condition for
approval of the plat, installation of a sanitary sewer that is larger than
necessary to meet the needs of the platted area, but necessary to complete the
City sanitary sewer system as it relates to both the area being platted and
other areas.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The subdivider must provide evidence of construction permits from the
Iowa Department of Natural Resources prior to approval of the final plat.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The above-mentioned facilities for the collection and disposal of
sanitary sewage from the platted area shall, upon final approval and acceptance
by the City, become the property of the City.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â The Cityâ€™s inability to efficiently collect or treat wastewater may be
grounds for rejection of a proposed subdivision. A proportional fee may be
requested by the City from the subdivider, to pay for the necessary upgrades in
the sewer system.
3.Â Â Â Water Drainage System; General. The subdivider of land being platted shall
install and construct a drainage system adequate to serve the area, including
anticipated extension of use to serve additional areas.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The water drainage system shall be separated from and independent of
any sanitary sewer system. The acceptable standard for sizing the drainage
system is to be able to handle the 100-year storm event without damage to
public or private property.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Drainage facilities shall be located in the road right-of-way where
feasible, or in perpetual unobstructed easements of appropriate width.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â In the drainage system design phase, the subdividerâ€™s engineer shall
study the effect of each subdivision on existing downstream drainage facilities
outside the area of the subdivision. The subdividerâ€™s drainage studies together
with such other studies as shall be appropriate shall serve as a guide to
needed improvements. Where it is anticipated that the additional runoff
incident to the development of the subdivision will overload an existing
downstream drainage facility, the Council may withhold approval of the
subdivision until provision has been made for the recovery of the cost for the
improvement of said potential condition in such sum as the Council shall
determine. No subdivision shall be approved unless adequate drainage will be
provided to an adequate drainage watercourse or facility.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â The Palo Technical Standards address and specify water quality volume
sizing criteria based on a one-inch average rainfall depth over the entire
site. Strictly in addition to this requirement, the developer shall provide for
infiltration practices that will satisfy volume requirements for an additional
zero-point five inch average rainfall depth over the entire site. The intent of
these infiltration practices is to further reduce stormwater runoff and improve
water quality treatment as merited by the challenging drainage conditions in
the City. The developer shall construct, protect, and maintain these areas for
three years or until fully established, whichever is longer, and which shall
not be disturbed by the property owner. When the City releases the developer
from this requirement, the property owner shall become responsible for
protecting and maintaining these areas in accordance with this chapter, the
Palo Technical Standards, and applicable State and federal law. No buildings,
structures, fences, play equipment, or kennels shall be permitted on all
drainage easement areas established to satisfy these additional infiltration
requirements. The subdivider should be aware that the City has unique drainage
issues and special care must be taken to avoid future water problems. Detention
basin ownership shall remain private to the lot owner.
4.Â Â Â Water Main System; General. The subdivider of land being platted shall
install and construct a water main system to adequately serve all lots or
parcels of land within the platted area, with due regard to the present and
reasonably foreseeable needs of the entire area, and shall connect the same to
the Cityâ€™s existing water mains. The water main system shall be in accordance
with SUDAS.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The subdivider shall install adequate water facilities, and fire
hydrants which shall be subject to SUDAS specifications and shall be subject
for review and approval by the Fire Chief. The location of all fire hydrants
shall be shown on the preliminary plat.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Under some circumstances the City may require, as a condition for
approval of the plat, installation of a water main that is larger than
necessary to meet the needs of the platted area, but necessary to complete the
City water distribution system as it relates to both the area being platted and
other areas. In such event the City may pay the subdivider the difference in
cost of pipe between the larger water main and the diameter of water main
reasonable to meet the foreseeable needs of the area.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The Cityâ€™s inability to generate, treat, or distribute water may be
grounds for rejection of a proposed subdivision. A proportional fee may be
requested by the City from the subdivider to pay for the necessary upgrades in
the water system.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â The water supply improvements shall, upon inspection, approval, and
acceptance by the City, become the property of the City.
5.Â Â Â Other Improvements. The owner and subdivider of the land being platted
shall be responsible for the installation of erosion control measures and the
installation of street lighting. All such improvements shall be under the
direction of the City Engineer.
6.Â Â Â Alternative Systems for Sewer and Water. Where connection to the City
sewer or water system cannot reasonably be made, the City Engineer may approve
alternate facilities for the distribution of water or the collection and
disposal of sanitary wastes or stormwater. Such alternate systems shall be
designed to fully protect the public health, safety, and welfare, and shall
meet all requirements of the State, County, or other applicable health
regulations. Prior to granting approval of such alternate systems, the owner
shall provide the City Engineer a waiver of assessment protest or such other
legally binding documents necessary to protect the City from the expense of the
subsequent installation of sewer or water facilities.
7.Â Â Â Street Lighting. New street lighting shall be installed within the right-
of-way of the overall boundary of the final plat. The developer/subdivider
shall be responsible for the preparation of a street lighting plan. Said street
lighting plan shall be reviewed and approved by the utility company servicing
said lights as well as the City Engineer. The costs associated with the
preparation of the plan and the design, fabrication and installation of the
streetlights shall be responsibility of the developer/subdivider. All
streetlights shall be designed for acceptable illuminance per current Design
Standards as specified in this Code of Ordinances. Allowable street lighting
fixtures shall be determined by the utility company servicing said lights.
8.Â Â Â Trees. The subdivider/developer shall be responsible for the installation
of a minimum of two trees per lot in both commercial and residential
subdivisions. All costs associated with installation shall be the
responsibility of the subdivider/developer. [See Section
151.02 and
165.19(10)]
170.12Â Â Â EASEMENTS REQUIRED.
1.Â Â Â Public Utilities. The flexible placement of easements for public utilities
shall be allowed; however, such placement shall be subject to the review of the
Council and all applicable utility companies prior to approval of the final
plat. All utilities to serve each lot of a subdivision shall be placed in a
common easement. Said easements shall be at least 10 feet in width. Easements
of greater width may be required along lot lines, or across lots when necessary
for the placement and maintenance of utilities. No buildings or structures,
except as necessary for utilities, shall be permitted on such easements.
2.Â Â Â Easements Along Streams and Watercourses. Wherever any stream or surface
watercourse is located in an area that is being subdivided, the subdivider
shall, at his or her own expense, make adequate provisions for the proper
drainage of surface water and shall provide and dedicate to the City an
easement equal to the floodway along said stream or water course to ensure the
proper maintenance of the watercourse, as approved by the City.
170.13Â Â Â MAINTENANCE BOND REQUIRED.
The owner and subdivider of the land being platted shall be required to provide
to the City proper maintenance bonds satisfactory to the City, so as to insure
that for a period of two years from the date of acceptance of any underground
improvement or four years from the date of acceptance of any above-ground
improvement, the owner and subdivider shall be responsible to maintain such
improvement in good repair. A performance bond will also be required per
Section
170.35.
170.14Â Â Â STANDARDS PRESCRIBED.
The standards set forth in this chapter shall be considered the minimum
standards necessary to protect the public health, safety, and general welfare.
These standards should also be considered in accordance with the requirements
of applicable State and federal agencies. In the event that the Cityâ€™s minimum
standards should conflict with applicable County, State, and federal
requirements, the County, State, and federal requirements shall prevail.
170.15Â Â Â LAND SUITABILITY.
No land shall be subdivided that is found to be unsuitable for subdividing by
reason of flooding, ponding, poor drainage, adverse soil conditions, adverse
geological formations, historic or archeological conflicts, unsatisfactory
topography, or other conditions likely to be harmful to the public health,
safety, or general welfare, unless such unsuitable conditions are corrected to
the satisfaction of the City. If land is found to be unsuitable for subdivision
for any of the reasons cited in this section, the Council shall state its
reasons in writing and afford the subdivider an opportunity to present data
refuting such unsuitability. Thereafter, the Council may reaffirm, modify, or
withdraw its determination regarding such unsuitability.
170.16Â Â Â LANDS SUBJECT TO FLOODING.
No subdivision containing land located in a floodway or a flood hazard area
shall be approved by the City unless it is demonstrated that the subdivision
complies with all requirements of the Cityâ€™s Floodplain Management Regulations.
No lot shall be located so as to include land located within a floodway or
flood hazard area unless the lot is of such size and shape that it will contain
a buildable area, not within the floodway or flood hazard area, suitable for
development as allowed by the zone in which the lot is located. Those areas
subject to flooding shall be determined by the U.S. Federal Emergency
Management Agency (FEMA) flood plain map for the City. Land located within a
flood hazard area or a floodway may be included within a plat as follows,
subject to the approval of the City.
1.Â Â Â Included within individual lots in the subdivision, subject to the
limitations of this section.
2.Â Â Â Reserved as open space for recreation use by all owners of lots in the
subdivision, with an appropriate legal instrument, approved by the City,
providing for its care and maintenance by such owners.
3.Â Â Â If acceptable to the City, dedicated to the City as public open space for
recreation or flood control purposes.
170.17Â Â Â PLAT TO CONFORM TO COMPREHENSIVE PLAN.
The arrangement, character, extent, width, grade, and location of all streets
shall conform to the specifications for such streets as approved by the
Council. The general nature and extent of the lots and uses proposed shall
conform to the Comprehensive Plan of the City, provided such plan has been
adopted by the City; and shall conform to such other plans, including but not
limited to a Major Street Plan, a Sanitary Sewer System Plan, or a Parks and
Open Space Plan, provided such plan has been adopted by the City.
170.18Â Â Â STREET STANDARDS.
1.Â Â Â General. The following standards shall apply to all streets to be located
within the subdivision:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Streets shall provide for the continuation of arterial and collector
streets from adjoining platted areas, and the extension of such streets into
adjoining unplatted areas. Where a plat encompasses the location for an
arterial or collector street proposed in the Comprehensive Plan or the Street
Plan, the plat shall provide for such street.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Street grades shall align to existing streets, and all grades for
streets shall be as approved by the City.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Arterial streets shall be located so as to not require direct access
from the arterial street to abutting lots.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â Street right-of-way widths and pavement widths shall be as specified in
the design standards for public improvements as defined by SUDAS.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â Half-streets are prohibited, except, where an existing platted half-
street abuts the subdivision, a platted half-street to complete the street
shall be required.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â Local streets should be designed to discourage through traffic while
safely connecting to collector or arterial streets.
Â Â Â G.Â Â Â Street jogs with center line offsets of less than one hundred 125 feet
shall be prohibited, except where topography, or other physical conditions make
such jogs unavoidable.
Â Â Â H.Â Â Â Streets shall intersect as nearly at right angles as possible; and no
street shall intersect any other street at less than 60 degrees.
Â Â Â I.Â Â Â Dead end streets are prohibited, except where a street is planned to
continue past the subdividerâ€™s property, a temporary dead end may be allowed.
Â Â Â J.Â Â Â Streets that connect with other streets, or loop streets, are
preferable for maintenance, fire protection, and circulation, but cul-de-sacs
may be permitted if there are no other feasible alternatives available. Cul-de-
sacs shall not exceed 600 feet in length unless a greater length is
unavoidable.
Â Â Â K.Â Â Â In general, alleys shall not be permitted in residential areas and
shall be required in commercial areas with normal street frontage. Dead end
alleys are prohibited, unless provided with a turn-around with a minimum right-
of- way diameter of 100 feet.
Â Â Â L.Â Â Â Alleys shall have a right-of-way of not less than 20 feet and a roadway
width of not less than 16 feet.
Â Â Â M.Â Â Â When a tract is subdivided into larger than normal lots or parcels,
such lots or parcels shall be so arranged as to permit the logical location and
opening of future streets and adequate utility connections. Easements for the
future openings and extensions for such streets or utilities may, at the
discretion of the Council, be made a requirement of the plat.
Â Â Â N.Â Â Â Streets that are or will become extensions of existing streets shall be
given the same name as the existing streets. New street names shall not be the
same or sound similar to existing street names. All street names shall be at
the approval of the Council.
Â Â Â O.Â Â Â Private streets shall be prohibited. The Council may approve a variance
to this rule where unusual conditions make a private street desirable, provided
adequate covenants or other legal documents ensure that the City will not have
or need to assume any maintenance or other responsibility for such street.
2.Â Â Â Minimum roadway and right-of-way standards defined by SUDAS.
3.Â Â Â Street Grades defined by SUDAS.
4.Â Â Â Street Surfacing and Improvements. After sewer, water, and other utilities
to be located underground within the right-of-way have been installed by the
subdivider, the subdivider shall construct a roadway to the following
standards:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â After sewer and water utilities have been installed by the developer,
the developer shall surface, or cause to be surfaced, roadways to the standards
prescribed in these regulations and the Palo Design Standards. At a minimum,
all surfacing shall be of a character as is suitable for expected traffic and
in harmony with similar improvements in surrounding areas. The type of pavement
shall be Portland cement concrete or, if approved by the City Engineer,
asphaltic cement equivalent. Adequate provision shall be made for culverts,
drains, and bridges. All road pavement, shoulders, drainage improvements, and
structures, curbs, turnarounds, and sidewalks shall conform to all construction
standards and specifications adopted by the Council and shall be incorporated
into the Plan of Improvement required to be submitted by the developer for plat
approval.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Any roadway constructed for commercial or industrial use is to be
constructed to meet the minimum recommended standards of the SUDAS, and is to
be reviewed by the City Engineer.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â The subgrade shall be scarified to a depth of eight inches below the
pavement, and compacted to 90 percent of modified proctor density.
5.Â Â Â Railroads and Limited Access Highways. Railroad rights-of-way and limited
access highways where so located as to affect the subdivision of adjoining
lands shall be treated as follows:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â In all districts a buffer strip at least 20 feet in depth in addition
to the normal depth of the lot required in the district shall be provided
adjacent to a limited access highway. This strip shall be part of the platted
lots and shall be designated on the plat: â€œThis strip is reserved for
screening. The placement of structures hereon is prohibited.â€
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Streets parallel to the railroad when intersecting a street which
crosses the railroad at grade shall, to the extent practicable, be at a
distance of at least 225 feet from the railroad right-of-way. Such distance
shall be determined with due consideration of the minimum distance required for
future separation of grades by means of appropriate approach gradients.
6.Â Â Â Sidewalks. Sidewalks are typically not required; however, if included in a
development, the following design standards shall apply to all subdividers in
accordance with SUDAS:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Sidewalks shall be a minimum of four feet in width except in the
Central Business District or in other areas specifically approved by the
Council of the City where the width may be greater. Sidewalks shall be located
one foot from the property line within the dedicated non-pavement right-of-way
of all streets.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Sidewalk Ramps. All sidewalks shall provide a curb ramp for
accommodation of the disabled at all intersections. Curb ramps shall be located
in line with the public sidewalk. Curb ramps shall comply with all requirements
for said ramps as set forth in the â€œAmericans With Disabilities Act.â€ Ramps
shall be sloped from the sidewalk intersection to the curb.
7.Â Â Â Driveways. The following standards shall apply to residential driveways in
accordance with SUDAS:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Residential driveways shall be a minimum width of 12 feet and a maximum
of 24 feet at the street.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Residential driveways shall be a minimum four-inch thick nonreinforced
Portland cement concrete.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Residential driveways shall be a minimum length from the structure to
the front lot line.
170.19Â Â Â BLOCK AND LOT STANDARDS.
The following standards shall apply to the layout of blocks and lots in all
subdivisions:
1.Â Â Â No residential block shall be longer than 1,300 feet or shorter than 300
feet measured from street line to street line. The width of blocks should be
arranged so as to allow two tiers of lots, with utility easement.
2.Â Â Â In blocks over 700 feet in length, the Council may require a public way or
an easement at least 25 feet in width, at or near the center of the block, for
use by pedestrians.
3.Â Â Â The size and shape of lots intended for commercial or industrial use shall
be adequate to provide for the use intended, and to meet the parking, loading,
and other requirements for such uses contained in the zoning ordinance.
4.Â Â Â Lot arrangement and design shall be such that all lots will provide
satisfactory building sites, properly related to topography and surrounding
land uses.
5.Â Â Â The size, area, minimum widths, and minimum depths of all lots shall
comply with all requirements of the zoning ordinance for the zone in which the
lot is located.
6.Â Â Â All lots shall abut a public street or an approved private street.
7.Â Â Â Unless unavoidable, lots shall not front, or have direct access to
arterial streets. Where unavoidable, lots shall be so arranged as to minimize
the number of access points.
8.Â Â Â All lot lines shall be at right angles to straight street lines or radial
to curved street lines, except where in the judgment of the Council a variation
to this provision will provide a better street and lot layout.
9.Â Â Â All lots shall conform to the yard requirements of the zoning ordinance
for the zone in which the lot is located.
10.Â Â Â Reversed frontage lots are prohibited. Double frontage lots shall only be
permitted where abutting a major street and a minor street, and such lots shall
front only on the minor street.
11.Â Â Â Lots shall provide for the future placement of accessory buildings
pursuant to the requirements of the zoning ordinance.
12.Â Â Â Lots on cul-de-sacs shall contain the minimum area as required in said
lotâ€™s district in accordance with SUDAS.
170.20Â Â Â PARKS AND OPEN SPACE.
All subdivisions should be so designed as to meet the neighborhood park and
open space needs of their residents. The following standards and procedures
will be used to determine the park and open space requirements for all proposed
residential developments or subdivisions greater than half acre in size within
the City:
1.Â Â Â For all residential developments and subdivisions, the subdivider shall be
responsible for providing adequate park and open space in one or both of the
following ways, depending on the decision of the City.
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â If it is feasible and compatible with the Comprehensive Plan, as
determined by the Council upon the recommendation of the Planning and Zoning
Commission and approved by the Council, the subdivider will be required to
dedicate and reserve an area for parks and open space, without cost to the
City.
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â The amount of land shall be determined by first calculating the
entire size of the land area of the proposed development as shown on the
preliminary plat or site plan and then to require dedication or reservation of
five percent of this amount for parks and open space.
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â This area shall be denoted on the final plat prior to approval of
the final plat.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Where such dedication is not feasible or compatible with the
Comprehensive Plan, as determined by the Council upon recommendation of the
Planning and Zoning Commission, the subdivider shall, in lieu thereof, pay to
the City a fee or combination of fee and land equivalent to the value of the
required dedication or reservation to be determined and used in the following
manner:
Â Â Â Â Â Â (1)Â Â Â The Council, upon recommendation of the Planning and Zoning
Commission, shall determine the size of the land area which it would have
required to set aside for parks and open space (five percent of the total land
area).
Â Â Â Â Â Â (2)Â Â Â The cash value of said land shall be determined by taking the total
purchase price or cost of all the land in the proposed subdivision and charge
the owner the proportionate value of the land area so designated, based upon
such purchase price or cost, provided such purchase price or cost is the
current fair and reasonable value of the land. If such purchase price or cost
does not reflect the current fair value of the land, the fair value of said
land shall be determined by an impartial appraisal, and in such manner as may
be designated by the Council, cost for said appraisal shall be paid the
subdivider.
Â Â Â Â Â Â (3)Â Â Â All funds so levied, assessed, and collected by the City shall be
deposited in a special fund to be known as the â€œSpecial Fund for the
Acquisition and Development of Public Service Areas, Open Space and
Recreational Facilities,â€ and that said funds so levied and collected shall be
used for such purposes at such places and in such a manner as shall be
approved, ordered and directed by a recreation committee appointed by the
Council. Any interest accumulated upon such funds shall be added to the
â€œSpecial Fundâ€ and be used only for acquisition and development of open space
and recreational facilities.
2.Â Â Â At the time of the preliminary plat approval, the Council, upon
recommendation by the Planning and Zoning Commission, shall determine whether
to require a dedication of land within the subdivision or the payment of a fee,
in lieu thereof, or a combination of both, from the subdivider, for parks and
open space.
3.Â Â Â Where a dedication is required, it shall be accomplished with a properly
executed warranty deed dedicating the required land to the City without cost to
the City. Where a fee, in lieu of dedication is required, the fee shall be
deposited with the Clerk. Whichever action is required, it shall be
accomplished prior to the approval of the final plat.
4.Â Â Â The determination by the City of whether to require dedication of land, or
a fee, in lieu thereof, shall be based on the following:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Recreational element of the Cityâ€™s Comprehensive Plan.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Topographic and geologic conditions and access and location of land in
subdivision available for dedication.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Size and shape of the subdivision and land available for dedication.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â The relation of the subdivision to the Comprehensive Plan map,
particularly as such plan map may show proposed public service areas, open
space, and recreational areas.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â The character and recreational needs of the neighborhood in which the
subdivision is located.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â The unsuitability in the subdivision for open space and recreational
purposes by reason of location, access, greater cost of development and
maintenance.
Â Â Â G.Â Â Â The possibility that land immediately adjoining the subdivision will
serve in whole or in part the public service area, open space, and recreational
needs of such subdivision.
Â Â Â H.Â Â Â Any and all other information relevant to a proper determination.
The determination of the Council as to whether land shall be dedicated or
reserved or a fee be charged, or a combination thereof, shall be final and
conclusive.
170.21Â Â Â PARKS SITES RESERVED.
When a tract being subdivided includes lands proposed to be parks in the
Comprehensive Plan or other official plan of the City, the subdivider shall
indicate such areas on the plat.
1.Â Â Â Proposed park sites shall be reserved for three years, giving the City or
other authorized public agency the option to purchase the land at the appraised
raw land value prior to the subdivision as established by a certified land
appraiser. The purchase price shall also include one-half of the cost for
grading and paving, including curbs, of the portion of any streets that are
contiguous to the site and any taxes and interest incurred by the subdivider
between the date of reservation and date of purchase by the public agency.
Should the park site not be purchased within three years, the subdivider may
then amend the final plat.
170.22Â Â Â NONRESIDENTIAL SUBDIVISIONS.
The following provisions shall apply to nonresidential subdivisions:
1.Â Â Â General. If a proposed subdivision includes land that is used for
commercial or industrial purpose, the layout of the subdivision with respect to
such land may be subject to additional provisions as the Council may require. A
nonresidential subdivision shall be subject to all the requirements of these
regulations, as well as such additional standards required by the Council, and
shall conform to the proposed land use and standards established in City plans
and regulations.
2.Â Â Â Standards. In addition to the principles and standards in these
regulations, which are appropriate to the planning of all subdivisions, the
subdivider shall demonstrate to the satisfaction of the City that the street,
parcel, and block pattern proposed are specifically adapted to the uses
anticipated and takes into account other uses in the vicinity. The following
principles and standards shall be observed:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â Proposed industrial or commercial parcels shall be suitable in area and
dimensions pursuant to those stated in the zoning ordinance.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â Street rights-of-way and pavement shall be adequate to accommodate the
type and volume of traffic anticipated to be generated thereupon.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Special requirements may be imposed by the City with respect to the
installation of public utilities, including water, sewer, and stormwater
drainage.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â Every effort shall be made to protect adjacent residential areas from
potential nuisance from a proposed commercial or industrial subdivision,
including the provision of extra depth in parcels backing up on existing or
potential residential development and provisions for a permanently landscaped
buffer strip when necessary.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â Streets carrying nonresidential traffic, especially truck traffic,
shall not normally be extended to the boundaries of adjacent existing or
potential residential areas.
170.23Â Â Â PRE-APPLICATION CONFERENCE.
Whenever a subdivision located within the platting jurisdiction of the City is
proposed, the owner and subdivider shall schedule a pre- application conference
with the Plats Officer. The conference should be attended by the Plats Officer
and such other City or utility representatives as are deemed desirable; and by
the owner and said ownerâ€™s engineer and/or planner, as deemed desirable. The
purpose of such conference shall be to acquaint the City with the proposed
subdivision, and to acquaint the subdivider with the requirements, procedures,
and any special problems relating to the proposed subdivision.
170.24Â Â Â SKETCH PLAN REQUIRED.
For the pre-application conference, the subdivider shall provide a map or
sketch showing the location of the subdivision, the general location of any
proposed streets and other improvements, and the general layout and arrangement
of intended land uses, in relation to the surrounding area.
170.25Â Â Â PRESENTATION TO PLANNING COMMISSION.
The subdivider may present the sketch plan to the Planning Commission for
review, prior to incurring significant costs preparing the preliminary or final
plat.
170.26Â Â Â SUBDIVISION CLASSIFIED.
Any proposed subdivision shall be classified as a minor subdivision or a major
subdivision.
1.Â Â Â Minor Subdivision. Any subdivision that contains not more than four lots
fronting on an existing street and that does not require construction of any
public improvements, and that does not adversely affect the remainder of the
parcel shall be classified as a minor plat.
2.Â Â Â Major Subdivision. Any subdivision that, in the opinion of the Council,
does not for any reason meet the definition of a minor subdivision, shall be
classified as a major subdivision.
170.27Â Â Â PLATS REQUIRED.
In order to secure approval of a proposed subdivision, the owner and subdivider
shall submit to the City, plats and other information as required by this
chapter. The owner and subdivider of any major subdivision shall comply with
the requirements for a preliminary plat and the requirements for a final plat.
The owner and subdivider of a minor subdivision may elect to submit a single
combined preliminary/final plat.
170.28Â Â Â REQUIREMENTS OF THE PRELIMINARY PLAT.
The subdivider shall prepare and file with the Clerk ten copies plus one
electronic copy of the preliminary plat, drawn at a scale of one inch equals
100 feet or larger. Sheet size shall not exceed 24 inches by 36 inches. Where
more than one sheet is required, the sheets shall show the number of the sheet
and the total number of sheets in the plat, and match lines indicating where
other sheets adjoin. The preliminary plat shall be clearly marked â€œPreliminary
Platâ€ and shall show, or have attached thereto, the following:
1.Â Â Â Title, scale, north point, and date
2.Â Â Â Proposed name of the subdivision that shall not duplicate or resemble
existing subdivision names in the City.
3.Â Â Â The name and address of the owner and the name, address and profession of
the person preparing the plan.
4.Â Â Â A key map showing the general location of the proposed subdivision in
relation to surrounding development.
5.Â Â Â The names and locations of adjacent subdivisions and the names of record
owners and location of adjoining parcels of unplatted land. A list of all
owners of record of property located within 200 feet of the subdivision
boundary shall be attached.
6.Â Â Â The location of property lines, streets and alleys, easements, buildings,
utilities, watercourses, tree masses, and other existing features affecting the
plat.
7.Â Â Â Existing and proposed zoning of the proposed subdivision and adjoining
property.
8.Â Â Â Contours at vertical intervals of not more than two feet if the general
slope of the site is less than 10 percent and at vertical intervals of not more
than five feet if the general slope is 10 percent or greater.
9.Â Â Â The legal description of the area being platted.
10.Â Â Â The boundary of the area being platted, shown as a dark line with the
approximate length of boundary lines and the approximate location of the
property in reference to known section lines.
11.Â Â Â The layout, numbers, and approximate dimension of proposed lots.
12.Â Â Â The location, width and dimensions of all streets and alleys proposed to
be dedicated for public use.
13.Â Â Â The proposed names for all streets in the area being platted.
14.Â Â Â Present and proposed utility systems, including sanitary and storm
sewers, other drainage facilities, water lines, gas mains, electric utilities,
cable utilities, telephone utilities and other facilities, and their
connections to existing utilities.
15.Â Â Â Proposed easements, showing locations, widths, purposes, and limitations.
16.Â Â Â Parcels of land proposed to be dedicated or reserved for schools, parks,
playgrounds, or other public, semi-public or community purposes, or shown for
such purpose in the Comprehensive Plan or other adopted plans.
17.Â Â Â A general summary description of any protective covenants or private
restrictions to be incorporated in the final plat.
18.Â Â Â Any other pertinent information, as necessary.
19.Â Â Â The fee, as required by this chapter.
20.Â Â Â All initial developments (phase one) and all future planned developments
within the area (phase two, phase three, etc.). Failure to completely identify
all proposed developments in the subdivision area will be grounds for rejecting
the plat.
170.29Â Â Â PROCEDURES FOR REVIEW OF PRELIMINARY PLATS.
1.Â Â Â The Clerk, upon receipt of ten copies plus one electronic copy of the
preliminary plat, shall file one copy in the records of the City, shall retain
one copy for public inspection.
2.Â Â Â The Plats Officer shall provide copies of the plat to the City Engineer,
City Attorney, City staff, and such other persons as necessary to review the
plat. After review comments are received from the City Engineer, the City
Attorney, and City staff and the applicant has considered the comments, the
Plat Officer shall schedule a plat for consideration by the Planning
Commission.
3.Â Â Â The Planning Commission shall examine the plat and the report of the City
Engineer, and such other information as it deems necessary or desirable, to
ascertain whether the plat conforms to the ordinances of the City, and conforms
to the Comprehensive Plan and other duly adopted plans of the City. The
Planning Commission shall, within 45 days of the filing of the plat with the
Clerk, forward a report and recommendation regarding the plat to the Council.
If such recommendation is to disapprove or modify the plat, the reasons
therefor shall be set forth in writing in the report, and a copy of the report
and recommendation shall be provided to the subdivider.
4.Â Â Â The Council shall examine the plat, the report of the City Engineer, the
report of the Planning Commission, and such other information as it deems
necessary or desirable. Upon such examination, the Council shall ascertain
whether the plat conforms to the ordinances and standards of the City, conforms
to the Comprehensive Plan and other duly adopted plans of the City, and will be
conducive to the orderly growth and development of the City in order to protect
the public health, safety, and welfare. Following such examination, the Council
may approve, approve subject to conditions, or disapprove the plat. If the
decision of the Council is to disapprove the plat, or to approve the plat
subject to conditions, the reasons therefor shall be set forth in writing in
the official records of the Council, and such decisions shall be provided to
the subdivider. Action on the preliminary plat by the Council shall be taken
within 60 days of the filing of the plat with the Clerk.
170.30Â Â Â DURATION OF APPROVAL OF PRELIMINARY PLAT.
The approval of a preliminary plat by the Council shall be valid for a period
of one year from the date of such approval; after which such approval shall be
void, and the subdivider shall take no action requiring the precedent approval
of a preliminary plat except upon application for and approval of an extension
of such period of validity, by the Council.
170.31Â Â Â AUTHORIZATION TO INSTALL IMPROVEMENTS.
The approval of the preliminary plat shall constitute authorization by the City
Staff for the installation of improvements as required by this chapter, and as
shown on the preliminary plat; provided no such improvement shall be
constructed or installed until and unless the plans, profiles, cross sections,
and specifications for the construction of such improvement have been submitted
to and approved in writing by, the City Engineer and all necessary permits have
been issued from the appropriate State and federal agencies (i.e., Iowa
Department of Natural Resources).
170.32Â Â Â TRANSFER OF LOTS WITHOUT CONSTRUCTING IMPROVEMENTS.
In the event the subdivider, its assigns, or successors in interest should
transfer lots in a subdivision without having constructed or installed the
pavement, water mains, sanitary sewer, storm sewers, sidewalks, or other public
improvements, the City shall have the right to install and construct such
improvements and the costs of such improvements shall be a lien and charge
against all the lots adjacent to or in front of which the improvements are made
and lots which may be assessed for improvements under the provisions of Chapter
384 of the Code of Iowa. The assessment for such improvements need not meet the
requirements of notice, benefit, or value as provided by State law for
assessing such improvements. In addition, the requirement to construct such
improvements is, and shall remain, a lien on all property located within the
subdivision until properly released by the City.
170.33Â Â Â COMPLETION AND ACCEPTANCE OF IMPROVEMENTS.
Before the Council will approve the final plat, all of the foregoing
improvements shall be constructed and accepted by formal resolution of the
Council. Before passage of said resolution of acceptance, the City Engineer
shall report that said improvements meet the City specifications and ordinances
or other City requirements, and the agreements between the subdivider and the
City.
170.34Â Â Â REQUIREMENT FOR DEVELOPERâ€™S AGREEMENT.
It is required for a developerâ€™s agreement at the preliminary plat stage, with
a review draft executed with each final plat.
170.35Â Â Â PERFORMANCE BOND PERMITTED.
In lieu of the requirement that improvements be completed prior to the approval
of a final plat, the subdivider may post a performance bond with the City,
guaranteeing that improvements not completed shall be completed within a period
of two years from the date of approval of such final plat; but such approval of
the plat shall not constitute final acceptance of any improvements to be
constructed. Improvements will be accepted only after their construction has
been completed.
170.36Â Â Â REQUIREMENTS OF THE FINAL PLAT.
The subdivider shall, within one year from the date of approval of the
preliminary plat, unless such time period has been extended or a performance
bond posted subject to Section
170.35, prepare and file with the Clerk, ten copies plus one electronic copy of
the final plat and required attachments, as set forth in this ordinance. Except
for a final plat for a minor subdivision as set forth herein, no final plat
shall be considered by the Council until and unless a preliminary plat for the
area included in the proposed final plat has been approved and has not expired
and become void as set forth above. The final plat shall be drawn at a scale of
one inch equals 100 feet or larger. Sheet size shall be no greater than 18
inches by 24 inches nor smaller than eight and one-half inches by 11 inches and
shall be of a size acceptable to the County Auditor. If more than one sheet is
used, each sheet shall clearly show the number of the sheet, the total number
of sheets included in the plat, and match lines indicating where other sheets
adjoin. The final plat shall be clearly marked â€œFinal Platâ€ and shall show the
following:
1.Â Â Â The name of the subdivision.
2.Â Â Â Name and address of the owner and subdivider.
3.Â Â Â Scale, and a graphic bar scale, north arrow, and date on each sheet.
4.Â Â Â All monuments to be of record, as required by Chapter 355, Code of Iowa.
5.Â Â Â Sufficient survey data to positively describe the bounds of every lot,
block, street, easement, or other area shown on the plat, as well as the outer
boundaries of the subdivided lands.
6.Â Â Â All distance, bearing, curve, and other survey data, as required by
Chapter 355, Code of Iowa.
7.Â Â Â All adjoining properties shall be identified, and where such adjoining
properties are a part of a recorded subdivision, the name of the subdivision
shall be shown. If the subdivision platted is part of a previously recorded
subdivision, sufficient ties shall be shown to controlling lines appearing on
the earlier plat to permit an overlay to be made.
8.Â Â Â Street names and clear designation of public alleys.
9.Â Â Â Block and lot numbers.
10.Â Â Â Accurate dimensions for any property to be dedicated or reserved for
public use, and the purpose for which such property is dedicated or reserved
for public use.
11.Â Â Â The purpose of any easement shown on the plat shall be confined to only
those easements pertaining to public utilities including gas, power, telephone,
cable television, water, sewer, easements for trails, bikeways, ingress and
egress, and such drainage easements as are deemed necessary for the orderly
development of the land encompassed within the plat.
12.Â Â Â All interior excepted parcels, clearly indicated and labeled, â€œnot a part
of this plat.â€
13.Â Â Â A strip of land shall not be reserved by the subdivider unless the land
is of sufficient size and shape to be of some practical use or service as
determined by the Council.
14.Â Â Â The minimum unadjusted acceptable error of closure for all subdivision
boundaries shall be 1:10,000 and shall be 1:5,000 for any individual lot.
15.Â Â Â A statement by a registered land surveyor that the plat was prepared by
the surveyor or under the surveyorâ€™s direct personal supervision, signed and
dated by the surveyor and bearing the surveyorâ€™s Iowa registration number or
seal.
16.Â Â Â A sign-off by the local public utility companies that the locale of
utility easements are properly placed for the installation of utilities.
17.Â Â Â A certification of dedication of streets and other public property and
perpetual easements for the installation, operation, and maintenance of
utilities.
18.Â Â Â Contain a signature block for the signature of the Mayor certifying the
Councilâ€™s approval of the plat.
19.Â Â Â Show any provisions provided by the Code of Iowa.
20.Â Â Â The final plat should also have the following accompanying instruments:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â A statement by the proprietors and their spouses, if any, that the plat
is prepared with their free consent and in accordance with their desire, signed
and acknowledged before an officer authorized to take the acknowledgments of
deeds. The statement by the proprietors may also include a dedication to the
public of all lands within the plat that are designated for streets, alleys,
parks, open areas, school property, or other public use, if the dedication is
approved by the Council.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â A statement from the mortgage holders or lien holders, if any, that the
plat is prepared with their free consent and in accordance with their desire,
signed and acknowledged before an officer authorized to take the acknowledgment
of deeds. An affidavit and bond as provided for in Section 354.12 of the Code
of Iowa may be recorded in lieu of the consent of the mortgage or lien holder.
When a mortgage or lien holder consents to the subdivision, a release of
mortgage or lien shall be recorded for any areas conveyed to the City or
dedicated to the public.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â An opinion by an attorney-at-law who has examined the abstract of title
of the land being platted. The opinion shall state the names of the proprietors
and holders of mortgages, liens or other encumbrances on the land being platted
and shall note the encumbrances, along with any bonds securing the
encumbrances. Utility easements shall not be construed to be encumbrances for
the purpose of this section.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â A certificate of the County Treasurer that the land is free from
certified taxes and certified special assessments or that the land is free from
certified taxes and that the certified special assessments are secured by bond
in compliance with Section 354.12 of the Code of Iowa.
Â Â Â E.Â Â Â A resolution and certificate for approval by the Council and for
signatures of the Mayor and Clerk.
Â Â Â F.Â Â Â A certificate from the County Auditor that the name or title of the
subdivision plat is approved by the County Auditor.
170.37Â Â Â VARIATIONS AND EXCEPTIONS.
The following shall apply to the granting of variances or exceptions:
1.Â Â Â Hardships. Where the Council finds that extraordinary hardships or
particular difficulties regarding the physical development of land may result
from strict compliance with these regulations, it may make variations or
exceptions to the regulations, except those required by State law, so that
substantial justice may be done and the public interest secured, provided that
such variation or exceptions to these regulations meets the following criteria:
Â Â Â A.Â Â Â The granting of the variation will not be detrimental to the public
safety, health, or welfare or injurious to other property or improvements in
the neighborhood in which the property is located.
Â Â Â B.Â Â Â The conditions upon which the request for a variation is based are
unique to the property for which the variation is sought, and are not
applicable, generally, to other property.
Â Â Â C.Â Â Â Because of the particular physical surroundings, shape or topographical
conditions of the specific property involved, a particular hardship to the
owner would result, as distinguished from a mere inconvenience, if the strict
letter of the regulations were carried out.
Â Â Â D.Â Â Â The purpose of the variation is not based exclusively upon a desire to
make more money out of the property.
2.Â Â Â Conditions. In granting variations and exceptions, the Council may require
such conditions as will, in its judgment, secure substantially the objectives
of the standards or requirements of these regulations.
3.Â Â Â Procedure for Variance. A petition for any such variation or exception
shall be submitted in writing by the developer at the time when the preliminary
plat is filed. The petition shall state fully the grounds for the application
and all of the facts relied upon by the petitioner.
170.38Â Â Â CHANGES AND AMENDMENTS.
Any provisions of these regulations may be changed and amended from time to
time by the Council, provided that such changes and amendments shall not become
effective until after a public hearing has been held, public notice of which
shall have been given as required by law. Such proposed amendments shall first
be submitted to the Planning Commission for study and recommendation before the
hearing date is scheduled. The Planning Commission shall forward its
recommendation to the Council within 30 days or a reasonable amount of time set
forth by the Council after the Council requests the recommendation. The Council
shall then give notice of and hold a public hearing on the proposed amendment.
